[38;2;248;248;242mZSHCOMPSYS(1)                    General Commands Manual                   ZSHCOMPSYS(1)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242mNAME[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       zshcompsys - zsh completion system[0m

[38;2;248;248;242mDESCRIPTION[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       This  describes  the  shell  code for the `new' completion system, referred to as[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       compsys.  It is written in shell functions based on  the  features  described  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       zshcompwid(1).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The  features  are  contextual,  sensitive  to  the  point at which completion is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       started.  Many completions are already provided.  For this  reason,  a  user  can[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       perform  a  great many tasks without knowing any details beyond how to initialize[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the system, which is described below in INITIALIZATION.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The context that decides what completion is to be performed may be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       •      an argument or option position: these describe the position on the command[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              line at which completion is requested.  For  example  `first  argument  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rmdir, the word being completed names a directory';[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       •      a special context, denoting an element in the shell's syntax.  For example[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `a word in command position' or `an array subscript'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       A full context specification contains other elements, as we shall describe.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Besides commands names and contexts, the system employs two more concepts, styles[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       and tags.  These provide ways for the user to configure the system's behaviour.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Tags  play  a  dual role.  They serve as a classification system for the matches,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       typically indicating a class of object that the user  may  need  to  distinguish.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       For  example,  when completing arguments of the ls command the user may prefer to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       try files before directories, so both of these are tags.  They also appear as the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       rightmost element in a context specification.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Styles modify various operations of the completion system, such as output format‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       ting, but also what kinds of completers are used (and in what  order),  or  which[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tags  are  examined.   Styles  may accept arguments and are manipulated using the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       zstyle command described in zshmodules(1).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       In summary, tags describe what the completion objects are, and style how they are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       to be completed.  At various points of execution, the  completion  system  checks[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       what  styles  and/or  tags  are defined for the current context, and uses that to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       modify its behavior.  The full description of context handling, which  determines[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       how  tags and other elements of the context influence the behaviour of styles, is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       described below in COMPLETION SYSTEM CONFIGURATION.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       When a completion is requested, a dispatcher function is called; see the descrip‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tion of _main_complete in the list of control functions  below.  This  dispatcher[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       decides which function should be called to produce the completions, and calls it.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       The result is passed to one or more completers, functions that implement individ‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       ual  completion  strategies: simple completion, error correction, completion with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       error correction, menu selection, etc.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       More generally, the shell functions contained in the completion system are of two[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       types:[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       •      those beginning `comp' are to be called directly; there are only a few  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              these;[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       •      those  beginning  `_'  are called by the completion code.  The shell func‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions of this set, which implement completion behaviour and may  be  bound[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to  keystrokes,  are  referred  to as `widgets'.  These proliferate as new[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completions are required.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242mINITIALIZATION[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       If the system was installed completely, it should be enough  to  call  the  shell[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       function  compinit from your initialization file; see the next section.  However,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the function compinstall can be run by a user to configure various aspects of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       completion system.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Usually, compinstall will insert code  into  .zshrc,  although  if  that  is  not[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       writable it will save it in another file and tell you that file's location.  Note[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       that  it  is  up  to you to make sure that the lines added to .zshrc are actually[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       run; you may, for example, need to move them to an earlier place in the  file  if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       .zshrc  usually  returns early.  So long as you keep them all together (including[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the comment lines at the start and finish), you can rerun compinstall and it will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       correctly locate and modify these lines.  Note, however, that any code you add to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       this section by hand is likely to be lost  if  you  rerun  compinstall,  although[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       lines using the command `zstyle' should be gracefully handled.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The  new  code  will  take effect next time you start the shell, or run .zshrc by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       hand; there is also an option to make them take effect immediately.  However,  if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       compinstall  has  removed  definitions, you will need to restart the shell to see[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the changes.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       To run compinstall you will need to make sure it is in a directory  mentioned  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       your  fpath  parameter, which should already be the case if zsh was properly con‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       figured as long as your startup files do not remove the  appropriate  directories[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       from  fpath.   Then  it  must  be autoloaded (`autoload -U compinstall' is recom‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       mended).  You can abort the installation any time you are being prompted for  in‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       formation,  and  your  .zshrc will not be altered at all; changes only take place[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       right at the end, where you are specifically asked for confirmation.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m   Use of compinit[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       This section describes the use of compinit to initialize completion for the  cur‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       rent  session when called directly; if you have run compinstall it will be called[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       automatically from your .zshrc.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       To initialize the system, the function compinit should be  in  a  directory  men‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tioned  in  the fpath parameter, and should be autoloaded (`autoload -U compinit'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       is recommended), and then run simply as `compinit'.  This will define a few util‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       ity functions, arrange for all the necessary shell functions  to  be  autoloaded,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       and will then re-define all widgets that do completion to use the new system.  If[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       you  use  the  menu-select  widget, which is part of the zsh/complist module, you[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       should make sure that that module is loaded before the call to compinit  so  that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       that  widget  is also re-defined.  If completion styles (see below) are set up to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       perform expansion as well as completion by default, and the TAB key is  bound  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       expand-or-complete,  compinit  will rebind it to complete-word; this is necessary[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       to use the correct form of expansion.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Should you need to use the original completion commands, you can still bind  keys[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       to  the  old  widgets  by  putting  a `.' in front of the widget name, e.g. `.ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       pand-or-complete'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       To speed up the running of compinit, it can be made to produce a dumped  configu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       ration  that  will be read in on future invocations; this is the default, but can[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       be turned off by calling compinit with the option -D.  The dumped file is .zcomp‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       dump in the same directory as the startup files (i.e. $ZDOTDIR or $HOME);  alter‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       natively, an explicit file name can be given by `compinit -d dumpfile'.  The next[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       invocation  of  compinit  will  read the dumped file instead of performing a full[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       initialization.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       If the number of completion files changes, compinit will recognise this and  pro‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       duce a new dump file.  However, if the name of a function or the arguments in the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       first  line  of a #compdef function (as described below) change, it is easiest to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       delete the dump file by hand so that compinit will re-create it the next time  it[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       is  run.  The check performed to see if there are new functions can be omitted by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       giving the option -C.  In this case the dump file will only be created  if  there[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       isn't one already.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The  dumping  is  actually  done by another function, compdump, but you will only[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       need to run this yourself if you change the configuration  (e.g.  using  compdef)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       and  then  want to dump the new one.  The name of the old dumped file will be re‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       membered for this purpose.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       If the parameter _compdir is set, compinit uses it as a directory  where  comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tion  functions  can  be found; this is only necessary if they are not already in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the function search path.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       For security reasons compinit also checks if  the  completion  system  would  use[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       files  not owned by root or by the current user, or files in directories that are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       world- or group-writable or that are not owned by root or by  the  current  user.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       If  such files or directories are found, compinit will ask if the completion sys‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tem should really be used.  To avoid these tests and make all files found be used[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       without asking, use the option -u, and to make compinit silently ignore all inse‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       cure files and directories use the option -i.  This security check is skipped en‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tirely when the -C option is given, provided the dumpfile exists.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The security check can be retried at any time by running the function  compaudit.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       This  is  the  same  check used by compinit, but when it is executed directly any[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       changes to fpath are made local to the function so they do not persist.  The  di‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       rectories  to be checked may be passed as arguments; if none are given, compaudit[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       uses fpath and _compdir to find completion  system  directories,  adding  missing[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       ones  to  fpath  as  necessary.  To force a check of exactly the directories cur‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       rently named in fpath, set _compdir to an empty string before  calling  compaudit[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       or compinit.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The function bashcompinit provides compatibility with bash's programmable comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tion  system.   When run it will define the functions, compgen and complete which[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       correspond to the bash builtins with the same names.  It will then be possible to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       use completion specifications and functions written for bash.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m   Autoloaded files[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       The convention for autoloaded functions used in completion  is  that  they  start[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       with  an underscore; as already mentioned, the fpath/FPATH parameter must contain[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the directory in which they are stored.  If zsh was properly  installed  on  your[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       system,  then fpath/FPATH automatically contains the required directories for the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       standard functions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       For incomplete installations, if compinit does not find  enough  files  beginning[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       with  an  underscore  (fewer than twenty) in the search path, it will try to find[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       more by adding the directory _compdir to the search path.  If that directory  has[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       a  subdirectory  named  Base, all subdirectories will be added to the path.  Fur‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       thermore, if the subdirectory Base has a subdirectory named Core,  compinit  will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       add  all  subdirectories of the subdirectories to the path: this allows the func‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tions to be in the same format as in the zsh source distribution.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       When compinit is run, it searches all such files accessible via  fpath/FPATH  and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       reads  the  first line of each of them.  This line should contain one of the tags[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       described below.  Files whose first line does not start with one  of  these  tags[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       are  not  considered  to be part of the completion system and will not be treated[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       specially.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The tags are:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       #compdef name ... [ -{p|P} pattern ... [ -N name ... ] ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The file will be made autoloadable and the function defined in it will  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              called  when  completing names, each of which is either the name of a com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mand whose arguments are to be completed or one of  a  number  of  special[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              contexts in the form -context- described below.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Each name may also be of the form `cmd=service'.  When completing the com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mand  cmd,  the  function  typically behaves as if the command (or special[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              context) service was being completed instead.  This provides a way of  al‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tering  the behaviour of functions that can perform many different comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions.  It is implemented by setting the parameter $service  when  calling[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the function; the function may choose to interpret this how it wishes, and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              simpler functions will probably ignore it.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the #compdef line contains one of the options -p or -P, the words fol‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              lowing are taken to be patterns.  The function will be called when comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion is attempted for a command or context that matches one  of  the  pat‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              terns.  The options -p and -P are used to specify patterns to be tried be‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fore  or  after  other  completions respectively.  Hence -P may be used to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              specify default actions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The option -N is used after a list following -p or -P; it  specifies  that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              remaining  words  no longer define patterns.  It is possible to toggle be‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tween the three options as many times as necessary.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       #compdef -k style key-sequence ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This option creates a widget behaving like the builtin  widget  style  and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              binds it to the given key-sequences, if any.  The style must be one of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              builtin   widgets   that   perform   completion,   namely   complete-word,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              delete-char-or-list,    expand-or-complete,     expand-or-complete-prefix,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              list-choices, menu-complete, menu-expand-or-complete, or reverse-menu-com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              plete.   If the zsh/complist module is loaded (see zshmodules(1)) the wid‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              get menu-select is also available.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              When one of the key-sequences is typed, the function in the file  will  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              invoked  to generate the matches.  Note that a key will not be re-bound if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              it already was (that is, was bound to something other than undefined-key).[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The widget created has the same name as the file and can be bound  to  any[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              other keys using bindkey as usual.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       #compdef -K widget-name style key-sequence [ name style seq ... ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is  similar  to -k except that only one key-sequence argument may be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              given for each widget-name style pair.  However, the entire set  of  three[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              arguments may be repeated with a different set of arguments.  Note in par‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ticular that the widget-name must be distinct in each set.  If it does not[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              begin  with `_' this will be added.  The widget-name should not clash with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the name of any existing widget: names based on the name of  the  function[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              are most useful.  For example,[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     #compdef -K _foo_complete complete-word "^X^C" \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       _foo_list list-choices "^X^D"[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              (all  on one line) defines a widget _foo_complete for completion, bound to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `^X^C', and a widget _foo_list for listing, bound to `^X^D'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       #autoload [ options ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Functions with the #autoload tag are marked for autoloading  but  are  not[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              otherwise  treated specially.  Typically they are to be called from within[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              one of the completion functions.  Any options supplied will be  passed  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  autoload  builtin;  a  typical  use is +X to force the function to be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              loaded immediately.  Note that the -U and -z flags are  always  added  im‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              plicitly.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The  # is part of the tag name and no white space is allowed after it.  The #com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       pdef tags use the compdef function described below; the main difference  is  that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the name of the function is supplied implicitly.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The special contexts for which completion functions can be defined are:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       -array-value-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The right hand side of an array-assignment (`name=(...)')[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       -assign-parameter-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The name of a parameter in an assignment, i.e. on the left hand side of an[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `='[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       -brace-parameter-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The name of a parameter expansion within braces (`${...}')[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       -command-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              A word in command position[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       -condition-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              A word inside a condition (`[[...]]')[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       -default-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Any word for which no other completion is defined[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       -equal-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              A word beginning with an equals sign[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       -first-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is  tried before any other completion function.  The function called[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              may set the _compskip parameter to one of various values: all: no  further[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion  is  attempted;  a string containing the substring patterns: no[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pattern completion functions will be called; a string containing  default:[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the function for the `-default-' context will not be called, but functions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              defined for commands will be.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       -math- Inside mathematical contexts, such as `((...))'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       -parameter-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The name of a parameter expansion (`$...')[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       -redirect-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The word after a redirection operator.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       -subscript-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The contents of a parameter subscript.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       -tilde-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              After an initial tilde (`~'), but before the first slash in the word.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       -value-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              On the right hand side of an assignment.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Default  implementations  are supplied for each of these contexts.  In most cases[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the context -context- is implemented by a corresponding  function  _context,  for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       example the context `-tilde-' and the function `_tilde').[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The  contexts  -redirect-  and  -value- allow extra context-specific information.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       (Internally, this is handled by the functions for each context calling the  func‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tion _dispatch.)  The extra information is added separated by commas.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       For  the  -redirect-  context,  the  extra  information  is  in  the form `-redi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       rect-,op,command', where op is the redirection operator and command is  the  name[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       of  the command on the line.  If there is no command on the line yet, the command[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       field will be empty.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       For the -value- context, the form is `-value-,name,command', where  name  is  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       name  of  the  parameter on the left hand side of the assignment.  In the case of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       elements of an associative array, for example `assoc=(key  <TAB>',  name  is  ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       panded  to  `name-key'.   In  certain  special contexts, such as completing after[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       `make CFLAGS=', the command part gives the name of the command, here make; other‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       wise it is empty.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       It is not necessary to define fully specific completions as  the  functions  pro‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       vided  will  try  to generate completions by progressively replacing the elements[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       with `-default-'.  For example, when completing after  `foo=<TAB>',  _value  will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       try  the  names  `-value-,foo,'  (note the empty command part), `-value-,foo,-de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       fault-' and`-value-,-default-,-default-', in that order, until it finds  a  func‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tion to handle the context.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       As an example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              compdef '_files -g "*.log"' '-redirect-,2>,-default-'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       completes  files  matching  `*.log' after `2> <TAB>' for any command with no more[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       specific handler defined.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Also:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              compdef _foo -value-,-default-,-default-[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       specifies that _foo provides completions for the values of parameters  for  which[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       no  special  function  has been defined.  This is usually handled by the function[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       _value itself.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The same lookup rules are used when looking up styles (as described  below);  for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       example[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              zstyle ':completion:*:*:-redirect-,2>,*:*' file-patterns '*.log'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       is  another  way  to  make  completion  after  `2> <TAB>' complete files matching[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       `*.log'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m   Functions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       The following function is defined by compinit and may be called directly.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       compdef [ -ane ] function name ... [ -{p|P} pattern ... [ -N name ...]][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       compdef -d name ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       compdef -k [ -an ] function style key-sequence [ key-sequence ... ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       compdef -K [ -an ] function name style key-seq [ name style seq ... ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The first form defines the function to call for completion  in  the  given[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              contexts as described for the #compdef tag above.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Alternatively,  all  the  arguments may have the form `cmd=service'.  Here[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              service should already have been defined by `cmd1=service' lines in  #com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pdef files, as described above.  The argument for cmd will be completed in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the same way as service.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  function argument may alternatively be a string containing almost any[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              shell code.  If the string contains an equal sign,  the  above  will  take[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              precedence.  The option -e may be used to specify the first argument is to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be  evaluated as shell code even if it contains an equal sign.  The string[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will be executed using the eval builtin command to  generate  completions.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  provides  a  way of avoiding having to define a new completion func‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion.  For example, to complete files ending in `.h' as arguments  to  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              command foo:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     compdef '_files -g "*.h"' foo[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  option -n prevents any completions already defined for the command or[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              context from being overwritten.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The option -d deletes any completion defined for the command  or  contexts[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              listed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  names  may  also  contain  -p, -P and -N options as described for the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              #compdef tag.  The effect on the argument list is identical, switching be‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tween definitions of patterns tried initially, patterns tried finally, and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              normal commands and contexts.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The parameter $_compskip may be set by any function defined for a  pattern[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              context.  If it is set to a value containing the substring `patterns' none[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of  the pattern-functions will be called; if it is set to a value contain‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ing the substring `all',  no  other  function  will  be  called.   Setting[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              $_compskip  in  this manner is of particular utility when using the -p op‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion, as otherwise the dispatcher will move  on  to  additional  functions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              (likely  the default one) after calling the pattern-context one, which can[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mangle the display of completion possibilities if not handled properly.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The form with -k defines a widget with the same name as the function  that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will be called for each of the key-sequences; this is like the #compdef -k[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tag.   The function should generate the completions needed and will other‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              wise behave like the builtin widget whose name is given as the style argu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ment.    The    widgets    usable    for    this    are:    complete-word,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              delete-char-or-list,     expand-or-complete,    expand-or-complete-prefix,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              list-choices,    menu-complete,    menu-expand-or-complete,    and     re‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              verse-menu-complete,  as well as menu-select if the zsh/complist module is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              loaded.  The option -n prevents the key being bound if it  is  already  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              bound to something other than undefined-key.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The form with -K is similar and defines multiple widgets based on the same[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function,  each  of  which requires the set of three arguments name, style[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and key-sequence, where the latter two are as for -k and the first must be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              a unique widget name beginning with an underscore.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Wherever applicable, the -a option makes the function autoloadable, equiv‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              alent to autoload -U function.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The function compdef can be used to associate existing completion functions  with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       new commands.  For example,[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              compdef _pids foo[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       uses the function _pids to complete process IDs for the command foo.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Note  also  the  _gnu_generic function described below, which can be used to com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       plete options for commands that understand the `--help' option.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242mCOMPLETION SYSTEM CONFIGURATION[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       This section gives a short overview of how the completion system works, and  then[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       more detail on how users can configure how and when matches are generated.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m   Overview[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       When  completion is attempted somewhere on the command line the completion system[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       begins building the context.  The context represents everything  that  the  shell[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       knows  about  the  meaning of the command line and the significance of the cursor[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       position.  This takes account of a number of things including  the  command  word[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       (such  as  `grep' or `zsh') and options to which the current word may be an argu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       ment (such as the `-o' option to zsh which takes a shell option as an argument).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The context starts out very generic ("we are beginning a completion") and becomes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       more specific as more is learned ("the current word is in a position that is usu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       ally a command name" or "the current word might be a variable name" and  so  on).[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       Therefore the context will vary during the same call to the completion system.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       This context information is condensed into a string consisting of multiple fields[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       separated  by colons, referred to simply as `the context' in the remainder of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       documentation.  Note that a user of the completion system rarely needs to compose[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       a context string, unless for example a new function is being written  to  perform[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       completion for a new command.  What a user may need to do is compose a style pat‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tern, which is matched against a context when needed to look up context-sensitive[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       options that configure the completion system.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The  next  few paragraphs explain how a context is composed within the completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       function suite.  Following that is discussion of how styles are defined.   Styles[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       determine  such  things  as how the matches are generated, similarly to shell op‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tions but with much more control.  They are defined with the zstyle builtin  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       mand (see zshmodules(1)).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The  context string always consists of a fixed set of fields, separated by colons[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       and with a leading colon before the first.  Fields which are not  yet  known  are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       left  empty,  but the surrounding colons appear anyway.  The fields are always in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the order :completion:function:completer:command:argument:tag.   These  have  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       following meaning:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       •      The  literal string completion, saying that this style is used by the com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pletion system.  This distinguishes the context from those  used  by,  for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              example, zle widgets and ZFTP functions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       •      The  function,  if  completion  is  called from a named widget rather than[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              through the normal completion system.  Typically this is blank, but it  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              set by special widgets such as predict-on and the various functions in the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Widget  directory  of the distribution to the name of that function, often[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in an abbreviated form.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       •      The completer currently active, the name of the function without the lead‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ing underscore and with other underscores converted to hyphens.   A  `com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleter'  is in overall control of how completion is to be performed; `com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              plete' is the simplest, but other  completers  exist  to  perform  related[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tasks such as correction, or to modify the behaviour of a later completer.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              See the section `Control Functions' below for more information.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       •      The command or a special -context-, just at it appears following the #com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pdef  tag or the compdef function.  Completion functions for commands that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              have sub-commands usually modify this field to contain  the  name  of  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              command  followed  by  a minus sign and the sub-command.  For example, the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion function for the cvs command sets this field  to  cvs-add  when[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completing arguments to the add subcommand.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       •      The  argument; this indicates which command line or option argument we are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completing.  For command arguments this generally  takes  the  form  argu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ment-n,  where  n  is the number of the argument, and for arguments to op‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions the form option-opt-n where n is the number of the argument  to  op‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion  opt.   However,  this is only the case if the command line is parsed[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with standard UNIX-style options and arguments, so many completions do not[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              set this.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       •      The tag.  As described previously, tags are used to  discriminate  between[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  types of matches a completion function can generate in a certain con‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              text.  Any completion function may use any tag name it likes, but  a  list[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of the more common ones is given below.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The  context  is  gradually  put together as the functions are executed, starting[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       with the main entry point, which adds :completion: and the  function  element  if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       necessary.   The  completer then adds the completer element.  The contextual com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       pletion adds the command and argument options.  Finally, the tag  is  added  when[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the types of completion are known.  For example, the context name[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              :completion::complete:dvips:option-o-1:files[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       says  that normal completion was attempted as the first argument to the option -o[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       of the command dvips:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              dvips -o ...[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       and the completion function will generate filenames.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Usually completion will be tried for all possible tags in an order given  by  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       completion  function.  However, this can be altered by using the tag-order style.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       Completion is then restricted to the list of given tags in the given order.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The _complete_help bindable command shows all the contexts and tags available for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       completion at a particular point.  This provides an easy way of finding  informa‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tion  for  tag-order  and other styles.  It is described in the section `Bindable[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       Commands' below.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       When looking up styles the completion system uses full context  names,  including[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the  tag.   Looking up the value of a style therefore consists of two things: the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       context, which is matched to the most specific (best fitting)  pattern,  and  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       name  of the style itself, which must be matched exactly.  The following examples[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       demonstrate that patterns may be loosely defined for styles that  apply  broadly,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       or as tightly defined as desired for styles that apply in narrower circumstances.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       For  example,  many  completion  functions can generate matches in a simple and a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       verbose form and use the verbose style to decide which form should be  used.   To[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       make all such functions use the verbose form, put[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              zstyle ':completion:*' verbose yes[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       in  a startup file (probably .zshrc).  This gives the verbose style the value yes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       in every context inside the completion system, unless that  context  has  a  more[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       specific  definition.   It is best to avoid giving the pattern as `*' in case the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       style has some meaning outside the completion system.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Many such general purpose styles can be configured simply by  using  the  compin‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       stall function.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       A  more specific example of the use of the verbose style is by the completion for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the kill builtin.  If the style is set, the builtin  lists  full  job  texts  and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       process command lines; otherwise it shows the bare job numbers and PIDs.  To turn[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the style off for this use only:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              zstyle ':completion:*:*:kill:*:*' verbose no[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       For  even  more control, the style can use one of the tags `jobs' or `processes'.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       To turn off verbose display only for jobs:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              zstyle ':completion:*:*:kill:*:jobs' verbose no[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The -e option to zstyle even allows completion function code to appear as the ar‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       gument to a style; this requires some understanding of the internals  of  comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tion functions (see see zshcompwid(1))).  For example,[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              zstyle -e ':completion:*' hosts 'reply=($myhosts)'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       This  forces  the  value  of the hosts style to be read from the variable myhosts[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       each time a host name is needed; this is useful  if  the  value  of  myhosts  can[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       change  dynamically.  For another useful example, see the example in the descrip‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tion of the file-list style below.  This form can be slow and should  be  avoided[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       for commonly examined styles such as menu and list-rows-first.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Note that the order in which styles are defined does not matter; the style mecha‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       nism  uses  the  most specific possible match for a particular style to determine[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the set of values.  Strings are preferred over patterns (for  example,  `:comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tion::complete:::foo'  is  more  specific  than `:completion::complete:::*'), and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       longer patterns are preferred over the pattern `*'. See zmodules(1) for details.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Context patterns that use something other than a wildcard (*) to match the middle[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       parts of the context -- the completer, command, and argument in :completion:func‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tion:completer:command:argument:tag -- should include all six colons (:)  explic‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       itly. Without this, a pattern such as :completion:*:foo:* could match foo against[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       a  component  other  than the intended one (for example, against completer when a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       match against command was intended).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Style names like those of tags are arbitrary and depend on the  completion  func‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tion.   However, the following two sections list some of the most common tags and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       styles.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m   Standard Tags[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       Some of the following are only used when looking up particular styles and do  not[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       refer to a type of match.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       accounts[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used to look up the users-hosts style[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       all-expansions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used by the _expand completer when adding the single string containing all[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              possible expansions[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       all-files[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for  the names of all files (as distinct from a particular subset, see the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              globbed-files tag).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       arguments[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for arguments to a command[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       arrays for names of array parameters[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       association-keys[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for keys of associative arrays; used when completing inside a subscript to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              a parameter of this type[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       bookmarks[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              when completing bookmarks (e.g. for URLs and the zftp function suite)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       builtins[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for names of builtin commands[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       characters[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for single characters in arguments of commands such as stty.    Also  used[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              when completing character classes after an opening bracket[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       colormapids[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for X colormap ids[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       colors for color names[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       commands[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for names of external commands.  Also used by complex commands such as cvs[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              when completing names subcommands.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       contexts[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for contexts in arguments to the zstyle builtin command[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       corrections[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used by the _approximate and _correct completers for possible corrections[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       cursors[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for cursor names used by X programs[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       default[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used  in  some  contexts to provide a way of supplying a default when more[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              specific tags are also valid.  Note that this tag is used  when  only  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function field of the context name is set[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       descriptions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used  when  looking  up the value of the format style to generate descrip‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions for types of matches[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       devices[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for names of device special files[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       directories[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for names of directories -- local-directories is used  instead  when  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleting arguments of cd and related builtin commands when the cdpath array[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is set[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       directory-stack[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for entries in the directory stack[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       displays[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for X display names[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       domains[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for network domains[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       email-plugin[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for email addresses from the `_email-plugin' backend of _email_addresses[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       expansions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used by the _expand completer for individual words (as opposed to the com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              plete  set  of  expansions)  resulting from the expansion of a word on the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              command line[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       extensions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for X server extensions[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       file-descriptors[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for numbers of open file descriptors[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       files  the generic file-matching tag used by functions completing filenames[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       fonts  for X font names[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       fstypes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for file system types (e.g. for the mount command)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       functions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              names of functions -- normally shell functions, although certain  commands[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              may understand other kinds of function[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       globbed-files[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for filenames when the name has been generated by pattern matching[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       groups for names of user groups[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       history-words[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for words from the history[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       hosts  for hostnames[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       indexes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for array indexes[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       interfaces[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for network interfaces[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       jobs   for jobs (as listed by the `jobs' builtin)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       keymaps[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for names of zsh keymaps[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       keysyms[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for names of X keysyms[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       libraries[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for names of system libraries[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       limits for system limits[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       local-directories[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for  names  of  directories that are subdirectories of the current working[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              directory when completing arguments of cd  and  related  builtin  commands[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              (compare  path-directories) -- when the cdpath array is unset, directories[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is used instead[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       mailboxes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for e-mail folders[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       manuals[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for names of manual pages[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       maps   for map names (e.g. NIS maps)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       messages[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used to look up the format style for messages[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       modifiers[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for names of X modifiers[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       modules[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for modules (e.g. zsh modules)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       my-accounts[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used to look up the users-hosts style[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       named-directories[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for named directories (you wouldn't have guessed that, would you?)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       names  for all kinds of names[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       newsgroups[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for USENET groups[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       nicknames[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for nicknames of NIS maps[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       options[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for command options[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       original[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used by the _approximate, _correct and _expand  completers  when  offering[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the original string as a match[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       other-accounts[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used to look up the users-hosts style[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       packages[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for packages (e.g. rpm or installed Debian packages)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       parameters[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for names of parameters[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       path-directories[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for names of directories found by searching the cdpath array when complet‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ing  arguments  of cd and related builtin commands (compare local-directo‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ries)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       paths  used to look up the values  of  the  expand,  ambiguous  and  special-dirs[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              styles[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       pods   for perl pods (documentation files)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       ports  for communication ports[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       prefixes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for prefixes (like those of a URL)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       printers[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for print queue names[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       processes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for process identifiers[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       processes-names[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used  to  look up the command style when generating the names of processes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for killall[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       sequences[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for sequences (e.g. mh sequences)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       sessions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for sessions in the zftp function suite[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       signals[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for signal names[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       strings[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for strings (e.g. the replacement strings for the cd builtin command)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       styles for styles used by the zstyle builtin command[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       suffixes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for filename extensions[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       tags   for tags (e.g. rpm tags)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       targets[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for makefile targets[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       time-zones[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for time zones (e.g. when setting the TZ parameter)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       types  for types of whatever (e.g. address types for the xhost command)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       urls   used to look up the urls and local styles when completing URLs[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       users  for usernames[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       values for one of a set of values in certain lists[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       variant[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used by _pick_variant to look up the command to run when determining  what[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              program is installed for a particular command name.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       visuals[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for X visuals[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       warnings[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used to look up the format style for warnings[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       widgets[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for zsh widget names[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       windows[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for IDs of X windows[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       zsh-options[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for shell options[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m   Standard Styles[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       Note that the values of several of these styles represent boolean values.  Any of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the strings `true', `on', `yes', and `1' can be used for the value `true' and any[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       of the strings `false', `off', `no', and `0' for the value `false'.  The behavior[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       for  any other value is undefined except where explicitly mentioned.  The default[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       value may be either `true' or `false' if the style is not set.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Some of these styles are tested first for every possible tag corresponding  to  a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       type  of match, and if no style was found, for the default tag.  The most notable[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       styles of this type are menu, list-colors and styles controlling completion list‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       ing such as list-packed and last-prompt.  When tested for the default  tag,  only[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the  function  field of the context will be set so that a style using the default[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tag will normally be defined along the lines of:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              zstyle ':completion:*:default' menu ...[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       accept-exact[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is tested for the default tag in addition to the tags valid  for  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              current  context.   If it is set to `true' and any of the trial matches is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the same as the string on the command line, this match will immediately be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              accepted (even if it would otherwise be considered ambiguous).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              When completing pathnames (where the tag used is `paths') this  style  ac‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cepts  any number of patterns as the value in addition to the boolean val‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ues.  Pathnames matching one of these patterns will  be  accepted  immedi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ately even if the command line contains some more partially typed pathname[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              components and these match no file under the directory accepted.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is also used by the _expand completer to decide if words begin‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ning with a tilde or parameter expansion should be expanded.  For example,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              if there are parameters foo and foobar, the string `$foo' will only be ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              panded  if  accept-exact is set to `true'; otherwise the completion system[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will be allowed to complete $foo to $foobar. If the style is set to  `con‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tinue',  _expand will add the expansion as a match and the completion sys‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tem will also be allowed to continue.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       accept-exact-dirs[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is used by filename completion.  Unlike accept-exact it is a boolean.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              By default, filename completion examines all components of a path  to  see[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              if  there are completions of that component, even if the component matches[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              an existing directory.  For example, when completion after /usr/bin/,  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function examines possible completions to /usr.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              When  this  style is `true', any prefix of a path that matches an existing[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              directory is accepted without any attempt to complete it further.   Hence,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in  the given example, the path /usr/bin/ is accepted immediately and com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pletion tried in that directory.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is also useful when completing after directories that magically[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              appear when referenced, such as ZFS .zfs directories or  NetApp  .snapshot[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              directories.  When the style is set the shell does not check for the exis‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tence of the directory within the parent directory.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  you  wish  to inhibit this behaviour entirely, set the path-completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              style (see below) to `false'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       add-space[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is used by the _expand completer.  If it  is  `true'  (the  de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fault), a space will be inserted after all words resulting from the expan‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sion,  or a slash in the case of directory names.  If the value is `file',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the completer will only add a space to names of existing files.  Either  a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              boolean  `true' or the value `file' may be combined with `subst', in which[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              case the completer will not add a space to words generated from the expan‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sion of a substitution of the form `$(...)' or `${...}'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The _prefix completer uses this style as a simple boolean value to  decide[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              if a space should be inserted before the suffix.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       ambiguous[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  applies  when  completing non-final components of filename paths, in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              other words those with a trailing slash.  If it is set, the cursor is left[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              after the first ambiguous component, even if menu completion  is  in  use.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The style is always tested with the paths tag.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       assign-list[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              When  completing  after an equals sign that is being treated as an assign‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ment, the completion system normally completes only one filename.  In some[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cases the value  may be a list of filenames separated by colons,  as  with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              PATH  and similar parameters.  This style can be set to a list of patterns[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matching the names of such parameters.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The default is to complete lists when the word on the  line  already  con‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tains a colon.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       auto-description[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  set,  this  style's  value will be used as the description for options[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              that are not described by the completion functions, but that have  exactly[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              one  argument.  The sequence `%d' in the value will be replaced by the de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              scription for this argument.  Depending on personal preferences, it may be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              useful to set this style to something like `specify: %d'.  Note that  this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              may not work for some commands.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       avoid-completer[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is  used  by the _all_matches completer to decide if the string con‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sisting of all matches should be added to the list currently being  gener‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ated.  Its value is a list of names of completers.  If any of these is the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              name  of  the completer that generated the matches in this completion, the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              string will not be added.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The default value for this style is `_expand _old_list _correct  _approxi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mate', i.e. it contains the completers for which a string with all matches[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will almost never be wanted.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       cache-path[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  style  defines the path where any cache files containing dumped com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pletion data  are  stored.   It  defaults  to  `$ZDOTDIR/.zcompcache',  or[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `$HOME/.zcompcache' if $ZDOTDIR is not defined.  The completion cache will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              not be used unless the use-cache style is set.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       cache-policy[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  style  defines the function that will be used to determine whether a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cache needs rebuilding.  See the section on  the  _cache_invalid  function[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              below.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       call-command[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is used in the function for commands such as make and ant where[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              calling  the command directly to generate matches suffers problems such as[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              being slow or, as in the case of make can potentially cause actions in the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              makefile to be executed. If it is set to `true' the command is  called  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              generate matches. The default value of this style is `false'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       command[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              In  many  places,  completion  functions need to call external commands to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              generate the list of completions.  This style can be used to override  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              command  that is called in some such cases.  The elements of the value are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              joined with spaces to form a command line to execute.  The value can  also[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              start  with a hyphen, in which case the usual command will be added to the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              end; this is most useful for putting `builtin' or `command'  in  front  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              make  sure  the appropriate version of a command is called, for example to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              avoid calling a shell function with the same name as an external command.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              As an example, the completion function for process  IDs  uses  this  style[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with  the  processes  tag  to generate the IDs to complete and the list of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              processes to display (if the verbose style is `true').  The list  produced[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              by  the  command should look like the output of the ps command.  The first[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              line is not displayed, but is searched for the string `PID' (or `pid')  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              find  the position of the process IDs in the following lines.  If the line[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              does not contain `PID', the first numbers in each of the other  lines  are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              taken as the process IDs to complete.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note that the completion function generally has to call the specified com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mand  for each attempt to generate the completion list.  Hence care should[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be taken to specify only commands that take a short time to  run,  and  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              particular to avoid any that may never terminate.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       command-path[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is a list of directories to search for commands to complete.  The de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fault for this style is the value of the special parameter path.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       commands[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is  used by the function completing sub-commands for the system ini‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tialisation scripts (residing in /etc/init.d or somewhere not too far away[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              from that).  Its values give the default commands to  complete  for  those[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              commands for which the completion function isn't able to find them out au‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tomatically.   The  default for this style are the two strings `start' and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `stop'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       complete[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is used by the _expand_alias function when invoked as a bindable com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mand.  If set to `true' and the word on the command line is not  the  name[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of an alias, matching alias names will be completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       complete-options[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is used by the completer for cd, chdir and pushd.  For these commands[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              a  -  is used to introduce a directory stack entry and completion of these[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is far more common than completing options.  Hence  unless  the  value  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              this  style is `true' options will not be completed, even after an initial[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              -.  If it is `true', options will be completed after an initial  -  unless[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              there is a preceding -- on the command line.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       completer[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The strings given as the value of this style provide the names of the com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleter  functions  to use. The available completer functions are described[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in the section `Control Functions' below.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Each string may be either the name of a completer function or a string  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  form  `function:name'.   In the first case the completer field of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              context will contain the name of the completer without the leading  under‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              score  and  with all other underscores replaced by hyphens.  In the second[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              case the function is the name of the completer to call,  but  the  context[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will  contain the user-defined name in the completer field of the context.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If the name starts with a hyphen, the string for the context will be build[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              from the name of the completer function as in the first case with the name[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              appended to it.  For example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' completer _complete _complete:-foo[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Here, completion will call the _complete completer twice, once using `com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              plete' and once using `complete-foo' in the completer field  of  the  con‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              text.   Normally, using the same completer more than once only makes sense[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              when used with the `functions:name' form, because  otherwise  the  context[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              name  will  be the same in all calls to the completer; possible exceptions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to this rule are the _ignored and _prefix completers.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The default value for this style is `_complete _ignored': only  completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will  be done, first using the ignored-patterns style and the $fignore ar‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ray and then without ignoring matches.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       condition[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is used by the _list completer function to decide if  insertion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of matches should be delayed unconditionally. The default is `true'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       delimiters[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  style is used when adding a delimiter for use with history modifiers[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              or glob qualifiers that have delimited arguments.  It is an array of  pre‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ferred  delimiters  to  add.   Non-special characters are preferred as the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion system may otherwise become confused.  The default list  is  :,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              +, /, -, %.  The list may be empty to force a delimiter to be typed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       disabled[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If this is set to `true', the _expand_alias completer and bindable command[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will try to expand disabled aliases, too.  The default is `false'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       domains[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              A  list  of  names of network domains for completion.  If this is not set,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              domain names will be taken from the file /etc/resolv.conf.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       environ[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The environ style is used when completing for `sudo'.  It is set to an ar‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ray of `VAR=value' assignments to be exported into the  local  environment[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              before the completion for the target command is invoked.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              zstyle ':completion:*:sudo::' environ \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                PATH="/sbin:/usr/sbin:$PATH" HOME="/root"[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       expand This  style  is used when completing strings consisting of multiple parts,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              such as path names.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If one of its values is the string `prefix', the partially typed word from[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the line will be expanded as far as possible even if trailing parts cannot[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If one of its values is the string `suffix', matching names for components[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              after the first ambiguous one will also be added.  This means that the re‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sulting string is the longest unambiguous string possible.  However,  menu[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion can be used to cycle through all matches.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       extra-verbose[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  set,  the completion listing is more verbose at the cost of a probable[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              decrease in completion speed.  Completion performance will suffer if  this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              style is set to `true'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       fake   This style may be set for any completion context.  It specifies additional[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              strings  that  will always be completed in that context.  The form of each[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              string is `value:description'; the colon and description may  be  omitted,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              but  any literal colons in value must be quoted with a backslash.  Any de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              scription provided is shown alongside the value in completion listings.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              It is important to use a sufficiently restrictive context when  specifying[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fake strings.  Note that the styles fake-files and fake-parameters provide[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              additional features when completing files or parameters.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       fake-always[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  works identically to the fake style except that the ignored-patterns[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              style is not applied to it.  This makes it possible to override a  set  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matches completely by setting the ignored patterns to `*'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  following  shows  a way of supplementing any tag with arbitrary data,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              but having it behave for display purposes like a separate  tag.   In  this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              example we use the features of the tag-order style to divide the named-di‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rectories  tag  into two when performing completion with the standard com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleter complete for arguments of cd.  The tag named-directories-normal be‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              haves as normal, but the tag named-directories-mine contains a  fixed  set[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of  directories.  This has the effect of adding the match group `extra di‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rectories' with the given completions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion::complete:cd:*' tag-order \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       'named-directories:-mine:extra\ directories[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       named-directories:-normal:named\ directories *'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion::complete:cd:*:named-directories-mine' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       fake-always mydir1 mydir2[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion::complete:cd:*:named-directories-mine' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       ignored-patterns '*'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       fake-files[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is used when completing files and looked up without a tag.  Its[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              values are of the form `dir:names...'.  This will add the  names  (strings[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              separated  by spaces) as possible matches when completing in the directory[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              dir, even if no such files really exist.  The dir may be a  pattern;  pat‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tern  characters  or colons in dir should be quoted with a backslash to be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              treated literally.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This can be useful on systems that  support  special  file  systems  whose[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              top-level pathnames can not be listed or generated with glob patterns (but[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              see  accept-exact-dirs  for  a more general way of dealing with this prob‐[0m
