[38;2;248;248;242m              lem).  It can also be used for directories for which  one  does  not  have[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              read permission.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  pattern form can be used to add a certain `magic' entry to all direc‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tories on a particular file system.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       fake-parameters[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is used by the completion function for parameter names.   Its  values[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              are  names of parameters that might not yet be set but should be completed[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              nonetheless.  Each name may also be followed by a colon and a string spec‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ifying the type of the parameter (like `scalar',  `array'  or  `integer').[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the  type  is  given, the name will only be completed if parameters of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              that type are required in the particular context.  Names for which no type[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is specified will always be completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       file-list[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style controls whether files completed  using  the  standard  builtin[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mechanism  are  to be listed with a long list similar to ls -l.  Note that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              this feature uses the shell module zsh/stat  for  file  information;  this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              loads  the  builtin  stat which will replace any external stat executable.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              To avoid this the following code can  be  included  in  an  initialization[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              file:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zmodload -i zsh/stat[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     disable stat[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  style  may  either be set to a `true' value (or `all'), or one of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              values `insert' or `list', indicating that files are to be listed in  long[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              format  in all circumstances, or when attempting to insert a file name, or[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              when listing file names without attempting to insert one.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              More generally, the value may be an array of any of the above values,  op‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tionally  followed by =num.  If num is present it gives the maximum number[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of matches for which long listing style will be used.  For example,[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' file-list list=20 insert=10[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              specifies that long format will be used when listing up to 20 files or in‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              serting a file with up to 10 matches (assuming a listing is to be shown at[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              all, for example on an ambiguous completion), else short  format  will  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle -e ':completion:*' file-list \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            '(( ${+NUMERIC} )) && reply=(true)'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              specifies  that  long  format  will be used any time a numeric argument is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              supplied, else short format.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       file-patterns[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is used by the standard function for  completing  filenames,  _files.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the  style is unset up to three tags are offered, `globbed-files',`di‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rectories' and `all-files', depending on the types of files   expected  by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  caller  of _files.  The first two (`globbed-files' and `directories')[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              are normally offered together to make  it  easier  to  complete  files  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sub-directories.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  file-patterns  style provides alternatives to the default tags, which[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              are not used.  Its value consists of elements of the  form  `pattern:tag';[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              each  string  may  contain  any number of such specifications separated by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              spaces.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The pattern is a pattern that is to be used to  generate  filenames.   Any[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              occurrence  of  the  sequence `%p' is replaced by any pattern(s) passed by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the function calling _files.  Colons in the pattern must be preceded by  a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              backslash  to make them distinguishable from the colon before the tag.  If[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              more than one pattern is needed, the patterns can be given inside  braces,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              separated by commas.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  tags  of  all strings in the value will be offered by _files and used[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              when looking up other styles.  Any tags in the same word will  be  offered[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              at  the  same  time  and  before  later  words.  If no `:tag' is given the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `files' tag will be used.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The tag may also be followed by an optional second colon  and  a  descrip‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion, which will be used for the `%d' in the value of the format style (if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              that is set) instead of the default description supplied by the completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function.  The inclusion of a description also gives precedence to associ‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ated options such as for completion grouping so it can be used where files[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              should be separated.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For  example,  to  make the rm command first complete only names of object[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              files and then the names of all files if there is no matching object file:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:*:rm:*:*' file-patterns \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         '*.o:object-files' '%p:all-files'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              To alter the default behaviour of file completion -- offer files  matching[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              a pattern and directories on the first attempt, then all files -- to offer[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              only  matching  files  on the first attempt, then directories, and finally[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              all files:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' file-patterns \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         '%p:globbed-files' '*(-/):directories' '*:all-files'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This works even where there is no  special  pattern:  _files  matches  all[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              files  using the pattern `*' at the first step and stops when it sees this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pattern.  Note also it will never try a pattern more than once for a  sin‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              gle completion attempt.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              To  separate  directories  into  a separate group from the files but still[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              complete them at the first attempt, a description needs to be given.  Note[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              that directories need to be explicitly excluded from the globbed-files be‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cause `*' will match directories. For grouping, it is  also  necessary  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              set the group-name style.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' file-patterns \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         '%p(^-/):globbed-files *(-/):directories:location'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              During  the execution of completion functions, the EXTENDED_GLOB option is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in effect, so the characters `#', `~' and `^' have special meanings in the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              patterns.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       file-sort[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The standard filename completion function uses this style without a tag to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              determine in which order the names should be listed; menu completion  will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cycle  through them in the same order.  The possible values are: `size' to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sort by the size of the file; `links' to sort by the number  of  links  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the file; `modification' (or `time' or `date') to sort by the last modifi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cation  time;  `access'  to  sort by the last access time; and `inode' (or[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `change') to sort by the last inode change time.  If the style is  set  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              any other value, or is unset, files will be sorted alphabetically by name.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the  value contains the string `reverse', sorting is done in the oppo‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              site order.  If the value contains the string `follow', timestamps are as‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sociated with the targets of symbolic links; the default  is  to  use  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              timestamps of the links themselves.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       file-split-chars[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              A  set  of  characters  that will cause all file completions for the given[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              context to be split at the point where any of the  characters  occurs.   A[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              typical  use is to set the style to :; then everything up to and including[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the last : in the string so far is ignored when completing files.  As this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is quite heavy-handed, it is usually preferable to update completion func‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions for contexts where this behaviour is useful.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       filter The ldap plugin of email address completion  (see  _email_addresses)  uses[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              this  style  to specify the attributes to match against when filtering en‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tries.  So for example, if the style is set  to  `sn',  matching  is  done[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              against  surnames.   Standard  LDAP filtering is used so normal completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matching is bypassed.  If this style  is  not  set,  the  LDAP  plugin  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              skipped.   You  may  also  need to set the command style to specify how to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              connect to your LDAP server.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       force-list[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This forces a list of completions to be shown at any point  where  listing[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is  done,  even  in cases where the list would usually be suppressed.  For[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              example, normally the list is only shown if there are at least two differ‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ent matches.  By setting this style to `always', the list will  always  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              shown,  even  if there is only a single match that will immediately be ac‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cepted.  The style may also be set to a number.  In  this  case  the  list[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will  be shown if there are at least that many matches, even if they would[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              all insert the same string.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is tested for the default tag as well as for each tag valid for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the current completion.  Hence the listing can be forced only for  certain[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              types of match.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       format If  this is set for the descriptions tag, its value is used as a string to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              display above matches in completion lists.   The  sequence  `%d'  in  this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              string  will  be  replaced  with a short description of what these matches[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              are.  This string may also contain the output attribute  sequences  under‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              stood by compadd -X (see zshcompwid(1)).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  style is tested with each tag valid for the current completion before[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              it is tested for the descriptions tag.  Hence different format strings can[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be defined for different types of match.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note also that some completer functions define  additional  `%'-sequences.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              These are described for the completer functions that make use of them.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Some  completion functions display messages that may be customised by set‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ting this style for the messages tag.  Here, the `%d' is replaced  with  a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              message given by the completion function.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Finally,  the  format  string  is looked up with the warnings tag, for use[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              when no matches could be generated at all.  In this case the `%d'  is  re‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              placed  with the descriptions for the matches that were expected separated[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              by spaces.  The sequence `%D' is replaced with the same descriptions sepa‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rated by newlines.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              It is possible to use printf-style field width specifiers  with  `%d'  and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              similar  escape sequences.  This is handled by the zformat builtin command[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              from the zsh/zutil module, see zshmodules(1).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       gain-privileges[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If set to true, this style enables the use of commands like sudo  or  doas[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to  gain extra privileges when retrieving information for completion. This[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is only done when a command such as sudo appears on the  command-line.  To[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              force  the use of, e.g. sudo or to override any prefix that might be added[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              due to gain-privileges, the command style can be used with  a  value  that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              begins with a hyphen.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       glob   This  is  used  by the _expand completer.  If it is set to `true' (the de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fault), globbing will be attempted on the words resulting from a  previous[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              substitution  (see  the substitute style) or else the original string from[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the line.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       global If this is set to `true' (the default), the  _expand_alias  completer  and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              bindable command will try to expand global aliases.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       group-name[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The  completion  system can group different types of matches, which appear[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in separate lists.  This style can be used to give the names of groups for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              particular tags.  For example, in command position the  completion  system[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              generates  names of builtin and external commands, names of aliases, shell[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              functions and parameters and reserved words as possible  completions.   To[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              have the external commands and shell functions listed separately:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:*:-command-:*:commands' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            group-name commands[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:*:-command-:*:functions' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            group-name functions[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              As  a  consequence,  any  match with the same tag will be displayed in the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              same group.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the name given is the empty string the name of the tag for the  matches[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will be used as the name of the group.  So, to have all different types of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matches displayed separately, one can just set:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' group-name ''[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              All  matches  for  which  no  group name is defined will be put in a group[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              named -default-.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              To display the group name in the output, see the format style (q.v.)   un‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              der the descriptions tag.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       group-order[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  style is additional to the group-name style to specify the order for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              display of the groups defined by that style (compare tag-order, which  de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              termines  which completions appear at all).  The groups named are shown in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the given order; any other groups are shown in the order  defined  by  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion function.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For example, to have names of builtin commands, shell functions and exter‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              nal commands appear in that order when completing in command position:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:*:-command-:*:*' group-order \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            builtins functions commands[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       groups A list of names of UNIX groups.  If this is not set, group names are taken[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              from the YP database or the file `/etc/group'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       hidden If  this  is  set  to  `true',  matches  for the given context will not be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              listed, although any description for the matches set with the format style[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will be shown.  If it is set to `all', not even the  description  will  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              displayed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note  that the matches will still be completed; they are just not shown in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the list.  To avoid having matches considered as possible  completions  at[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              all, the tag-order style can be modified as described below.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       hosts  A  list  of  names of hosts that should be completed.  If this is not set,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              hostnames are taken from the file `/etc/hosts'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       hosts-ports[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is used by commands that need or accept hostnames  and  network[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ports.  The strings in the value should be of the form `host:port'.  Valid[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ports  are determined by the presence of hostnames; multiple ports for the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              same host may appear.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       ignore-line[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is tested for each tag valid for the current completion.   If  it  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              set to `true', none of the words that are already on the line will be con‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sidered  as possible completions.  If it is set to `current', the word the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cursor is on will not be considered as a possible completion.   The  value[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `current-shown'  is similar but only applies if the list of completions is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              currently shown on the screen.  Finally, if the style is set  to  `other',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              all words on the line except for the current one will be excluded from the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              possible completions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  values  `current'  and `current-shown' are a bit like the opposite of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the accept-exact style:  only strings with missing characters will be com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleted.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note that you almost certainly don't want to set this to `true' or `other'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for a general context such as `:completion:*'.  This is because  it  would[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              disallow  completion  of,  for example, options multiple times even if the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              command in question accepts the option more than once.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       ignore-parents[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The style is tested without a tag by the function completing pathnames  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              order to determine whether to ignore the names of directories already men‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tioned  in the current word, or the name of the current working directory.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The value must include one or both of the following strings:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              parent The name of any directory whose path is already  contained  in  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     word  on  the  line is ignored.  For example, when completing after[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     foo/../, the directory foo will not be considered a  valid  comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     tion.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              pwd    The  name  of  the current working directory will not be completed;[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     hence, for example, completion after ../ will not use the  name  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     the current directory.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In addition, the value may include one or both of:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              ..     Ignore  the  specified  directories  only when the word on the line[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     contains the substring `../'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              directory[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     Ignore the specified directories only when names of directories are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     completed, not when completing names of files.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Excluded values act in a similar fashion to values of the ignored-patterns[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              style, so they can be restored to consideration by the _ignored completer.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       ignored-patterns[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              A list of patterns; any trial completion matching one of the patterns will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be excluded from consideration.  The _ignored completer can appear in  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              list of completers to restore the ignored matches.  This is a more config‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              urable version of the shell parameter $fignore.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note  that the EXTENDED_GLOB option is set during the execution of comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion functions, so the characters `#', `~' and `^' have  special  meanings[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in the patterns.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       insert This  style is used by the _all_matches completer to decide whether to in‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sert the list of all matches unconditionally instead of adding the list as[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              another match.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       insert-ids[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              When completing process IDs, for example as arguments to the kill and wait[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              builtins the name of a command may be converted to the appropriate process[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ID.  A problem arises when the process name typed is not unique.   By  de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fault (or if this style is set explicitly to `menu') the name will be con‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              verted  immediately  to a set of possible IDs, and menu completion will be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              started to cycle through them.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the value of the style is `single', the shell will wait until the  user[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              has  typed enough to make the command unique before converting the name to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              an ID; attempts at completion will be unsuccessful until that  point.   If[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  value  is  any other string, menu completion will be started when the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              string typed by the user is longer than the common prefix  to  the  corre‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sponding IDs.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       insert-sections[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is used with tags of the form `manuals.X' when completing names[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of manual pages. If set and the X in the tag name matches the section num‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ber of the page being completed, the section number is inserted along with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the page name. For example, given[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:manuals.*' insert-sections true[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              man ssh_<TAB> may be completed to man 5 ssh_config.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The value may also be set to one of `prepend', or `suffix'.  `prepend' be‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              haves  the  same  as  `true' as in the above example, while `suffix' would[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              complete man ssh_<TAB> as man ssh_config.5.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This is especially useful in conjunction with separate-sections, as it en‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sures that the page requested of man corresponds to the one  displayed  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  completion  listing  when there are multiple pages with the same name[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              (e.g., printf(1) and printf(3)).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The default for this style is `false'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       insert-tab[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If this is set to `true', the completion system will insert a TAB  charac‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ter  (assuming  that  was  used to start completion) instead of performing[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion when there is no non-blank character to the left of the cursor.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If it is set to `false', completion will be done even there.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The value may also contain the substrings `pending' or `pending=val'.   In[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              this  case,  the typed character will be inserted instead of starting com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pletion when there is unprocessed input pending.  If a val is given,  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pletion will not be done if there are at least that many characters of un‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              processed input.  This is often useful when pasting characters into a ter‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              minal.   Note  however,  that  it relies on the $PENDING special parameter[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              from the zsh/zle module being set properly which is not guaranteed on  all[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              platforms.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  default  value  of  this style is `true' except for completion within[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              vared builtin command where it is `false'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       insert-unambiguous[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is used by the _match and _approximate completers.  These  completers[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              are  often  used with menu completion since the word typed may bear little[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              resemblance to the final completion.  However, if this  style  is  `true',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  completer  will  start menu completion only if it could find no unam‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              biguous initial string at least as long as the original  string  typed  by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the user.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In the case of the _approximate completer, the completer field in the con‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              text  will already have been set to one of correct-num or approximate-num,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              where num is the number of errors that were accepted.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In the case of the _match completer, the style may  also  be  set  to  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              string  `pattern'.   Then  the pattern on the line is left unchanged if it[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              does not match unambiguously.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       keep-prefix[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is used by the _expand completer.  If it is  `true',  the  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleter  will  try  to keep a prefix containing a tilde or parameter expan‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sion.  Hence, for example, the string `~/f*' would be expanded to  `~/foo'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              instead  of  `/home/user/foo'.   If the style is set to `changed' (the de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fault), the prefix will only be left unchanged if there were other changes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              between the expanded words and the original word from  the  command  line.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Any other value forces the prefix to be expanded unconditionally.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  behaviour of _expand when this style is `true' is to cause _expand to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              give up when a single expansion with the restored prefix is  the  same  as[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the original; hence any remaining completers may be called.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       known-hosts-files[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style should contain a list of files to search for host names and (if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  use-ip  style  is  set)  IP addresses in a format compatible with ssh[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              known_hosts files.  If it is not set, the  files  /etc/ssh/ssh_known_hosts[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and ~/.ssh/known_hosts are used.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       last-prompt[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is  a more flexible form of the ALWAYS_LAST_PROMPT option.  If it is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `true', the completion system will try to return the cursor to the  previ‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ous command line after displaying a completion list.  It is tested for all[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tags  valid  for the current completion, then the default tag.  The cursor[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will be moved back to the previous line if this style is  `true'  for  all[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              types  of  match.   Note that unlike the ALWAYS_LAST_PROMPT option this is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              independent of the numeric argument.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       list   This style is used by the _history_complete_word bindable command.  If  it[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is  set  to `true' it has no effect.  If it is set to `false' matches will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              not be listed.  This overrides the  setting  of  the  options  controlling[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              listing  behaviour,  in  particular  AUTO_LIST.  The context always starts[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with `:completion:history-words'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       list-colors[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If the zsh/complist module is loaded, this style can be used to set  color[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              specifications.   This  mechanism  replaces  the use of the ZLS_COLORS and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ZLS_COLOURS parameters described in the section `The zsh/complist  Module'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in zshmodules(1), but the syntax is the same.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  this  style  is  set for the default tag, the strings in the value are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              taken as specifications that are to be used everywhere.  If it is set  for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              other  tags,  the specifications are used only for matches of the type de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              scribed by the tag.  For this to work best, the group-name style  must  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              set to an empty string.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In  addition  to  setting styles for specific tags, it is also possible to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              use group names specified explicitly by the group-name tag  together  with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  `(group)' syntax allowed by the ZLS_COLORS and ZLS_COLOURS parameters[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and simply using the default tag.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              It is possible to use any color specifications already set up for the  GNU[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              version of the ls command:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:default' list-colors \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            ${(s.:.)LS_COLORS}[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  default  colors are the same as for the GNU ls command and can be ob‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tained by setting the style to an empty string (i.e. '').[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       list-dirs-first[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is used by file completion and corresponds to a particular setting of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the file-patterns style.  If set, the default directories to be  completed[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              are listed separately from and before completion for other files.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       list-grouped[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  this  style is `true' (the default), the completion system will try to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              make certain completion listings more compact by  grouping  matches.   For[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              example,  options  for commands that have the same description (shown when[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the verbose style is set to `true') will appear as a single  entry.   How‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ever, menu selection can be used to cycle through all the matches.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       list-packed[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is  tested  for each tag valid in the current context as well as the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              default tag.  If it is set to `true', the corresponding matches appear  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              listings  as if the LIST_PACKED option were set.  If it is set to `false',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              they are listed normally.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       list-prompt[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If this style is set for the default tag, completion lists that don't  fit[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              on  the  screen  can  be scrolled (see the description of the zsh/complist[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              module in zshmodules(1)).  The value, if not the  empty  string,  will  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              displayed after every screenful and the shell will prompt for a key press;[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              if the style is set to the empty string, a default prompt will be used.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  value  may  contain the escape sequences: `%l' or `%L', which will be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              replaced by the number of the last line displayed and the total number  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              lines;  `%m'  or  `%M',  the number of the  last match shown and the total[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              number of matches; and `%p' and `%P', `Top' when at the beginning  of  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              list,  `Bottom'  when at the end and the position shown as a percentage of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the total length otherwise.  In each case the form with the uppercase let‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ter will be replaced by a string of fixed width, padded to the  right with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              spaces, while the lowercase form will be  replaced  by  a  variable  width[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              string.   As  in  other  prompt  strings, the escape sequences `%S', `%s',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `%B', `%b', `%U', `%u' for entering and leaving the display  modes  stand‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              out, bold and underline, and `%F', `%f', `%K', `%k' for changing the fore‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ground background colour, are also available, as is the form `%{...%}' for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              enclosing escape sequences which display with zero (or, with a numeric ar‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              gument, some other) width.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              After deleting this prompt the variable LISTPROMPT should be unset for the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              removal to take effect.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       list-rows-first[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  style  is tested in the same way as the list-packed style and deter‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mines whether matches are to be listed in a rows-first fashion as  if  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              LIST_ROWS_FIRST option were set.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       list-separator[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The  value  of  this  style  is used in completion listing to separate the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              string to complete from a description when possible (e.g. when  completing[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              options).  It defaults to `--' (two hyphens).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       list-suffixes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  style  is  used  by the function that completes filenames.  If it is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `true', and completion is attempted on a string containing  multiple  par‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tially  typed pathname components, all ambiguous components will be shown.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Otherwise, completion stops at the first ambiguous component.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       local  This is for use with functions that complete URLs  for  which  the  corre‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sponding  files  are  available  directly from the file system.  Its value[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              should consist of three strings: a hostname, the path to the  default  web[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pages  for  the  server, and the directory name used by a user placing web[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pages within their home area.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' local toast \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         /var/http/public/toast public_html[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Completion after `http://toast/stuff/' will look for files in  the  direc‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tory     /var/http/public/toast/stuff,      while     completion     after[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `http://toast/~yousir/' will look for files in the directory  ~yousir/pub‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              lic_html.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       mail-directory[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  set,  zsh will assume that mailbox files can be found in the directory[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              specified.  It defaults to `~/Mail'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       match-original[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is used by the _match completer.  If it is set to only,  _match  will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              try  to  generate  matches without inserting a `*' at the cursor position.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If set to any other non-empty value, it will first try to generate matches[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              without inserting the `*' and if that yields no matches, it will try again[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with the `*' inserted.  If it is unset or set to the empty string,  match‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ing will only be performed with the `*' inserted.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       matcher[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is tested separately for each tag valid in the current context.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Its  value  is  placed  before  any  match  specifications  given  by  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matcher-list style so can override them via the use of  an  x:  specifica‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion.   The  value should be in the form described in the section `Comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion Matching Control' in zshcompwid(1).  For examples of  this,  see  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              description of the tag-order style.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For  notes comparing the use of this and the matcher-list style, see under[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the description of the tag-order style.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       matcher-list[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style can be set to a list of match specifications that are to be ap‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              plied everywhere. Match specifications are described in the section  `Com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pletion  Matching  Control'  in zshcompwid(1).  The completion system will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              try them one after another for each completer selected.  For  example,  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              try first simple completion and, if that generates no matches, case-insen‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sitive completion:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' matcher-list '' 'm:{a-zA-Z}={A-Za-z}'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              By  default  each  specification  replaces the previous one; however, if a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              specification is prefixed with +, it is added to the existing list.  Hence[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              it is possible to create increasingly general specifications without repe‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tition:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' matcher-list \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            '' '+m:{a-z}={A-Z}' '+m:{A-Z}={a-z}'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              It is possible to create match specifications valid  for  particular  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleters  by  using  the  third field of the context.  This applies only to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completers that override the global matcher-list, which as of this writing[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              includes only _prefix and _ignored.  For example, to  use  the  completers[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _complete  and  _prefix  but  allow  case-insensitive completion only with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _complete:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' completer _complete _prefix[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:complete:*:*:*' matcher-list \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            '' 'm:{a-zA-Z}={A-Za-z}'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              User-defined names, as explained for the completer style,  are  available.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  makes it possible to try the same completer more than once with dif‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ferent match specifications each time.  For example, to try normal comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion without a match specification, then normal completion  with  case-in‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sensitive matching, then correction, and finally partial-word completion:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' completer \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         _complete _correct _complete:foo[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:complete:*:*:*' matcher-list \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         '' 'm:{a-zA-Z}={A-Za-z}'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:foo:*:*:*' matcher-list \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         'm:{a-zA-Z}={A-Za-z} r:|[-_./]=* r:|=*'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the  style  is unset in any context no match specification is applied.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Note also that some completers such as _correct and  _approximate  do  not[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              use  the  match  specifications  at all, though these completers will only[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ever be called once even if the matcher-list contains more than  one  ele‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ment.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Where  multiple specifications are useful, note that the entire completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is done for each element of matcher-list, which  can  quickly  reduce  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              shell's  performance.  As a rough rule of thumb, one to three strings will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              give  acceptable  performance.   On  the  other  hand,  putting   multiple[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              space-separated  values  into the same string does not have an appreciable[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              impact on performance.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If there is no current matcher or it is empty, and the option NO_CASE_GLOB[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is in effect, the matching for files is  performed  case-insensitively  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              any  case.   However, any matcher must explicitly specify case-insensitive[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matching if that is required.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For notes comparing the use of this and the matcher style, see  under  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              description of the tag-order style.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       max-errors[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is  used by the _approximate and _correct completer functions to de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              termine the maximum number of errors to allow.  The completer will try  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              generate  completions by first allowing one error, then two errors, and so[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              on, until either a match or matches were found or the  maximum  number  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              errors given by this style has been reached.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the  value for this style contains the string `numeric', the completer[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function will take any numeric argument as the maximum  number  of  errors[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              allowed. For example, with[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:approximate:::' max-errors 2 numeric[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              two errors are allowed if no numeric argument is given, but with a numeric[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              argument of six (as in `ESC-6 TAB'), up to six errors are accepted.  Hence[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with  a  value  of `0 numeric', no correcting completion will be attempted[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              unless a numeric argument is given.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the value contains the string `not-numeric', the completer will not try[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to generate corrected completions when given a  numeric  argument,  so  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              this  case  the number given should be greater than zero.  For example, `2[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              not-numeric' specifies that correcting completion  with  two  errors  will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              usually  be performed, but if a numeric argument is given, correcting com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pletion will not be performed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The default value for this style is `2 numeric'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       max-matches-width[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is used to determine the trade off between  the  width  of  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              display  used  for  matches and the width used for their descriptions when[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the verbose style is in effect.  The value gives  the  number  of  display[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              columns  to reserve for the matches.  The default is half the width of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              screen.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This has the most impact when several matches have  the  same  description[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and  so  will  be  grouped together.  Increasing the style will allow more[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matches to be grouped together; decreasing it will allow more of  the  de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              scription to be visible.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       menu   If  this  is `true' in the context of any of the tags defined for the cur‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rent completion menu completion will be used.  The value  for  a  specific[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tag will take precedence over that for the `default' tag.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  none of the values found in this way is `true' but at least one is set[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to `auto', the shell behaves as if the AUTO_MENU option is set.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If one of the values is explicitly set to `false', menu completion will be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              explicitly turned off, overriding the MENU_COMPLETE option and other  set‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tings.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In the form `yes=num', where `yes' may be any of the `true' values (`yes',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `true',  `on'  and `1'), menu completion will be turned on if there are at[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              least num matches.  In the form `yes=long', menu completion will be turned[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              on if the list does not fit on the screen.  This does  not  activate  menu[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion if the widget normally only lists completions, but menu comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion  can  be activated in that case with the value `yes=long-list' (Typi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cally, the value `select=long-list' described later is more useful  as  it[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              provides control over scrolling.)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Similarly, with any of the `false' values (as in `no=10'), menu completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will not be used if there are num or more matches.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  value  of this widget also controls menu selection, as implemented by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the zsh/complist module.  The following values may appear either alongside[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              or instead of the values above.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the value contains the string `select', menu selection will be  started[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              unconditionally.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In the form `select=num', menu selection will only be started if there are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              at  least num matches.  If the values for more than one tag provide a num‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ber, the smallest number is taken.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Menu selection can be turned off explicitly by defining a value containing[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the string`no-select'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              It is also possible to start menu selection only if the  list  of  matches[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              does  not  fit  on  the screen by using the value `select=long'.  To start[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              menu selection even if the current widget only performs listing,  use  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              value `select=long-list'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              To turn on menu completion or menu selection when there are a certain num‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ber  of matches or the list of matches does not fit on the screen, both of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `yes=' and `select=' may be given twice, once with a number and once  with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `long' or `long-list'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Finally,  it  is possible to activate two special modes of menu selection.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The word `interactive' in the value causes interactive mode to be  entered[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              immediately  when  menu  selection  is started; see the description of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              zsh/complist module in zshmodules(1)  for  a  description  of  interactive[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mode.   Including the string `search' does the same for incremental search[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mode.   To  select  backward  incremental  search,  include   the   string[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `search-backward'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       muttrc If set, gives the location of the mutt configuration file.  It defaults to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `~/.muttrc'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       numbers[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is used with the jobs tag.  If it is `true', the shell will complete[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              job numbers instead of the shortest unambiguous prefix of the job  command[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              text.   If  the  value  is a number, job numbers will only be used if that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              many words from the job descriptions are required to resolve  ambiguities.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              For  example,  if  the value is `1', strings will only be used if all jobs[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              differ in the first word on their command lines.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       old-list[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is used by the _oldlist completer.  If it is set  to  `always',  then[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              standard  widgets  which  perform  listing will retain the current list of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matches, however they were generated; this can be  turned  off  explicitly[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with  the  value  `never',  giving the behaviour without the _oldlist com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleter.  If the style is unset, or any other value, then the existing list[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of completions is displayed if it is not already; otherwise, the  standard[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion  list  is generated; this is the default behaviour of _oldlist.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              However, if there is an old list and this style contains the name  of  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completer function that generated the list, then the old list will be used[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              even if it was generated by a widget which does not do listing.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For  example,  suppose you type ^Xc to use the _correct_word widget, which[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              generates a list of corrections for the word under the  cursor.   Usually,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              typing  ^D  would  generate a standard list of completions for the word on[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the command line, and show that.  With _oldlist, it will instead show  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              list of corrections already generated.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              As  another  example  consider the _match completer: with the insert-unam‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              biguous style set to `true' it inserts only a  common  prefix  string,  if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              there  is any.  However, this may remove parts of the original pattern, so[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              that further completion could produce more matches than on the  first  at‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tempt.   By using the _oldlist completer and setting this style to _match,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the list of matches generated on the first attempt will be used again.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       old-matches[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is used by the _all_matches completer to decide if  an  old  list  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matches  should  be  used  if  one exists.  This is selected by one of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `true'  values  or  by  the  string  `only'.   If  the  value  is  `only',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _all_matches  will  only  use an old list and won't have any effect on the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              list of matches currently being generated.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If this style is set it is generally unwise to call the _all_matches  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleter  unconditionally.  One possible use is for either this style or the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completer style to be defined with the -e option to  zstyle  to  make  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              style conditional.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       old-menu[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is  used by the _oldlist completer.  It controls how menu completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              behaves when a completion has already been inserted and the user  types  a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              standard completion key such as TAB.  The default behaviour of _oldlist is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              that  menu  completion  always continues with the existing list of comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions.  If this style is set to `false',  however,  a  new  completion  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              started  if  the old list was generated by a different completion command;[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              this is the behaviour without the _oldlist completer.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For example, suppose you type ^Xc to generate a list of  corrections,  and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              menu  completion  is  started  in one of the usual ways.  Usually, or with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              this style set to `false', typing TAB at this point would start trying  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              complete  the line as it now appears.  With _oldlist, it instead continues[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to cycle through the list of corrections.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       original[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is used by the _approximate and _correct completers to decide if  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              original  string should be added as a possible completion.  Normally, this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is done only if there are at least two possible corrections, but  if  this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              style  is  set to `true', it is always added.  Note that the style will be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              examined with the completer field in the context name set  to  correct-num[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              or approximate-num, where num is the number of errors that were accepted.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       packageset[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is used when completing arguments of the Debian `dpkg' program.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              It  contains  an override for the default package set for a given context.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              For example,[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:complete:dpkg:option--status-1:*' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                                    packageset avail[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              causes available packages, rather than only installed packages, to be com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleted for `dpkg --status'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       path   The function that completes color names uses this style  with  the  colors[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tag.  The value should be the pathname of a file containing color names in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  format of an X11 rgb.txt file.  If the style is not set but this file[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is found in one of various standard locations it will be used as  the  de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fault.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       path-completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is used by filename completion.  By default, filename completion ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              amines all components of a path to see if there are  completions  of  that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              component.  For example, /u/b/z can be completed to /usr/bin/zsh.  Explic‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              itly setting this style to `false' inhibits this behaviour for path compo‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              nents  up  to  the  / before the cursor; this overrides the setting of ac‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cept-exact-dirs.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Even with the style set to `false', it is still possible to complete  mul‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tiple  paths  by setting the option COMPLETE_IN_WORD and moving the cursor[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              back to the first component in the path to  be  completed.   For  example,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              /u/b/z can be completed to /usr/bin/zsh if the cursor is after the /u.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       pine-directory[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  set,  specifies the directory containing PINE mailbox files.  There is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              no default, since recursively searching this directory is inconvenient for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              anyone who doesn't use PINE.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       ports  A list of Internet service names (network ports) to complete.  If this  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              not set, service names are taken from the file `/etc/services'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       prefix-hidden[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is used for certain completions which share a common prefix, for ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ample command options beginning with dashes.  If it is `true', the  prefix[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will not be shown in the list of matches.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The default value for this style is `false'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       prefix-needed[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  style  is  also relevant for matches with a common prefix.  If it is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              set to `true' this common prefix must be typed by the user to generate the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matches.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The style is applicable to the options, signals, jobs, functions, and  pa‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rameters completion tags.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For command options, this means that the initial `-', `+', or `--' must be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              typed explicitly before option names will be completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For  signals,  an initial `-' is required before signal names will be com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleted.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For jobs, an initial `%' is required before job names will be completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For function and parameter names, an initial `_' or `.' is required before[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function or parameter names starting with those characters  will  be  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleted.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  default  value  for  this style is `false' for function and parameter[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completions, and  `true' otherwise.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       preserve-prefix[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is used when completing path names.  Its value should be a pat‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tern matching an initial prefix of the word to  complete  that  should  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              left  unchanged  under  all circumstances.  For example, on some Unices an[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              initial `//' (double slash) has a special meaning; setting this  style  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  string `//' will preserve it.  As another example, setting this style[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to `?:/' under Cygwin would allow completion after `a:/...' and so on.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       range  This is used by the  _history  completer  and  the  _history_complete_word[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              bindable command to decide which words should be completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  it  is a single number, only the last N words from the history will be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If it is a range of the form `max:slice', the last  slice  words  will  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completed;  then  if  that yields no matches, the slice words before those[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will be tried and so on.  This process stops  either  when  at  least  one[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              match has been found, or max words have been tried.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The default is to complete all words from the history at once.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       recursive-files[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  this  style  is  set,  its  value is an array of patterns to be tested[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              against `$PWD/': note the trailing slash, which allows directories in  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pattern  to be delimited unambiguously by including slashes on both sides.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If an ordinary file completion fails and the word on the command line does[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              not yet have a directory part to its name, the style  is  retrieved  using[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  same  tag  as  for  the  completion just attempted, then the elements[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tested against $PWD/ in turn.  If one matches, then the  shell  reattempts[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion  by prepending the word on the command line with each directory[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in the expansion of **/*(/) in turn.  Typically the elements of the  style[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will  be set to restrict the number of directories beneath the current one[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to a manageable number, for example `*/.git/*'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For example,[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' recursive-files '*/zsh/*'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the current directory is /home/pws/zsh/Src,  then  zle_tr<TAB>  can  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completed to Zle/zle_tricky.c.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       regular[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  style  is  used by the _expand_alias completer and bindable command.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If set to `true' (the default), regular aliases will be expanded but  only[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in  command position.  If it is set to `false', regular aliases will never[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be expanded.   If it is set to `always', regular aliases will be  expanded[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              even if not in command position.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       rehash If this is set when completing external commands, the internal list (hash)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of commands will be updated for each search by issuing the rehash command.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              There  is  a  speed penalty for this which is only likely to be noticeable[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              when directories in the path have slow file access.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       remote-access[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If set to `false', certain commands will be prevented from making Internet[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              connections to retrieve remote information.  This includes the  completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for the CVS command.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              It  is  not always possible to know if connections are in fact to a remote[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              site, so some may be prevented unnecessarily.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       remove-all-dups[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The _history_complete_word bindable command and the _history completer use[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              this to decide if all duplicate matches should  be  removed,  rather  than[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              just consecutive duplicates.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       select-prompt[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  this  is  set  for the default tag, its value will be displayed during[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              menu selection (see the menu style above) when the  completion  list  does[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              not fit on the screen as a whole.  The same escapes as for the list-prompt[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              style  are  understood, except that the numbers refer to the match or line[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the mark is on.  A default prompt is used when  the  value  is  the  empty[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              string.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       select-scroll[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  style  is tested for the default tag and determines how a completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              list is scrolled during a menu selection (see the menu style  above)  when[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  completion  list does not fit on the screen as a whole.  If the value[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is `0' (zero), the list is scrolled by half-screenfuls; if it is  a  posi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tive  integer, the list is scrolled by the given number of lines; if it is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              a negative number, the list is scrolled by a screenful minus the  absolute[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              value  of  the  given number of lines.  The default is to scroll by single[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              lines.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       separate-sections[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This style is used with the manuals tag when completing  names  of  manual[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pages.   If  it  is `true', entries for different sections are added sepa‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rately using tag names of the form `manuals.X', where  X  is  the  section[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              number.  When the group-name style is also in effect, pages from different[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sections  will  appear separately.  This style is also used similarly with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the words style when completing words for  the  dict  command.  It  allows[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              words from different dictionary databases to be added separately. See also[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              insert-sections.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The default for this style is `false'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       show-ambiguity[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the zsh/complist module is loaded, this style can be used to highlight[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the first ambiguous character in completion lists. The value is  either  a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              color indication such as those supported by the list-colors style or, with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              a  value of `true', a default of underlining is selected. The highlighting[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is only applied if the completion display strings correspond to the actual[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matches.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       show-completer[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Tested whenever a new completer is tried.  If it is `true', the completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              system outputs a progress message in the listing area  showing  what  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleter is being tried.  The message will be overwritten by any output when[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completions are found and is removed after completion is finished.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       single-ignored[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is  used by the _ignored completer when there is only one match.  If[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              its value is `show', the single match will be displayed but not  inserted.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the value is `menu', then the single match and the original string are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              both added as matches and menu completion is started, making  it  easy  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              select either of them.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       sort   This allows the standard ordering of matches to be overridden.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  its value is `true' or `false', sorting is enabled or disabled.  Addi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tionally the values associated with the `-o' option to compadd can also be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              listed: match, nosort, numeric, reverse.  If it is not set  for  the  con‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              text, the standard behaviour of the calling widget is used.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  style is tested first against the full context including the tag, and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              if that fails to produce a value against the context without the tag.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In many cases where a calling widget explicitly selects a  particular  or‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              dering  in lieu of the default, a value of `true' is not honoured.  An ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ample of where this is not the case is for command history where  the  de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fault  of sorting matches chronologically may be overridden by setting the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              style to `true'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In the _expand completer, if it is set to `true', the expansions generated[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will always be sorted.  If it is set to `menu', then  the  expansions  are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              only  sorted when they are offered as single strings but not in the string[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              containing all possible expansions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       special-dirs[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Normally, the completion code will not produce the directory names `.' and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `..' as possible completions.  If this style is set to `true', it will add[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              both `.' and `..' as possible completions; if it is set to `..', only `..'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will be added.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The following example sets special-dirs to `..' when the current prefix is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              empty, is a single `.', or consists only of a path beginning  with  `../'.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Otherwise the value is `false'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle -e ':completion:*' special-dirs \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                        '[[ $PREFIX = (../)#(|.|..) ]] && reply=(..)'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       squeeze-slashes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  set  to `true', sequences of slashes in filename paths (for example in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `foo//bar') will be treated as a single slash.  This is the  usual  behav‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              iour  of UNIX paths.  However, by default the file completion function be‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              haves as if there were a `*' between the slashes.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       stop   If set to `true', the _history_complete_word bindable  command  will  stop[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              once  when  reaching  the beginning or end of the history.  Invoking _his‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tory_complete_word will then wrap around to the opposite end of  the  his‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tory.   If  this  style  is  set  to  `false' (the default), _history_com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              plete_word will loop immediately as in a menu completion.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       strip-comments[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If set to `true', this style causes non-essential comment text to  be  re‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              moved  from completion matches.  Currently it is only used when completing[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              e-mail addresses where it removes any display  name  from  the  addresses,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cutting them down to plain user@host form.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       subst-globs-only[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is used by the _expand completer.  If it is set to `true', the expan‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sion  will only be used if it resulted from globbing; hence, if expansions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              resulted from the use of the substitute style described below,  but  these[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              were not further changed by globbing, the expansions will be rejected.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The default for this style is `false'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       substitute[0m
