[38;2;248;248;242m              This  boolean  style controls whether the _expand completer will first try[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to expand all substitutions in the string (such as `$(...)' and `${...}').[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The default is `true'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       suffix This is used by the _expand completer if the word starts with a  tilde  or[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              contains  a  parameter  expansion.   If it is set to `true', the word will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              only be expanded if it doesn't have a suffix, i.e. if it is something like[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `~foo' or `$foo' rather than `~foo/' or `$foo/bar', unless that suffix it‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              self contains characters eligible for expansion.   The  default  for  this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              style is `true'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       tag-order[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This provides a mechanism for sorting how the tags available in a particu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              lar context will be used.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  values  for the style are sets of space-separated lists of tags.  The[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tags in each value will be tried at the same time; if no match  is  found,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  next value is used.  (See the file-patterns style for an exception to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              this behavior.)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:complete:-command-:*:*' tag-order \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         'commands functions'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              specifies that completion in command position first offers  external  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mands and shell functions.  Remaining tags will be tried if no completions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              are found.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In  addition  to  tag  names, each string in the value may take one of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              following forms:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -      If any value consists of only a hyphen, then only the  tags  speci‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     fied  in the other values are generated.  Normally all tags not ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     plicitly selected are tried last if the specified tags fail to gen‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     erate any matches.  This means that a single value consisting  only[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     of a single hyphen turns off completion.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              ! tags...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     A  string starting with an exclamation mark specifies names of tags[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     that are not to be used.  The effect is the same as  if  all  other[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     possible tags for the context had been listed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              tag:label ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     Here,  tag  is  one  of the standard tags and label is an arbitrary[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     name.  Matches are generated as normal but the name label  is  used[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     in  contexts  instead of tag.  This is not useful in words starting[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     with !.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     If the label starts with a hyphen, the tag is prepended to the  la‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     bel to form the name used for lookup.  This can be used to make the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     completion  system try a certain tag more than once, supplying dif‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     ferent style settings for each attempt; see below for an example.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              tag:label:description[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     As before, but description will replace the `%d' in  the  value  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     the format style instead of the default description supplied by the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     completion function.  Spaces in the description must be quoted with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     a  backslash.  A `%d' appearing in description is replaced with the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     description given by the completion function.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In any of the forms above the tag may be a pattern or several patterns  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  form  `{pat1,pat2...}'.   In this case all matching tags will be used[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              except for any given explicitly in the same string.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              One use of these features is to try one tag more than once, setting  other[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              styles  differently  on  each attempt, but still to use all the other tags[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              without having to repeat them all.  For example,  to  make  completion  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function  names  in  command  position ignore all the completion functions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              starting with an underscore the first time completion is tried:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:*:-command-:*:*' tag-order \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         'functions:-non-comp *' functions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:functions-non-comp' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         ignored-patterns '_*'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              On the first attempt, all tags will be offered but the functions tag  will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be  replaced by functions-non-comp.  The ignored-patterns style is set for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              this tag to exclude functions starting with an underscore.  If  there  are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              no  matches,  the  second  value of the tag-order style is used which com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pletes functions using the default tag, this time presumably including all[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function names.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The matches for one tag can be split into different groups.  For example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' tag-order \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         'options:-long:long\ options[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                          options:-short:short\ options[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                          options:-single-letter:single\ letter\ options'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:options-long' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                          ignored-patterns '[-+](|-|[^-]*)'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:options-short' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                          ignored-patterns '--*' '[-+]?'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:options-single-letter' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                          ignored-patterns '???*'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              With the group-names style set, options beginning with `--',  options  be‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ginning  with  a single `-' or `+' but containing multiple characters, and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              single-letter options will be displayed in separate groups with  different[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              descriptions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Another  use of patterns is to try multiple match specifications one after[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              another.  The matcher-list style  offers  something  similar,  but  it  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tested very early in the completion system and hence can't be set for sin‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              gle  commands  nor  for more specific contexts.  Here is how to try normal[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion without any match  specification  and,  if  that  generates  no[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matches,  try again with case-insensitive matching, restricting the effect[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to arguments of the command foo:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:*:foo:*:*' tag-order '*' '*:-case'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*-case' matcher 'm:{a-z}={A-Z}'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              First, all the tags offered when completing after foo are tried using  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              normal  tag  name.   If  that  generates  no  matches, the second value of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tag-order is used, which tries all tags again except that this  time  each[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              has  -case appended to its name for lookup of styles.  Hence this time the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              value for the matcher style from the second call to zstyle in the  example[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is used to make completion case-insensitive.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              It is possible to use the -e option of the zstyle builtin command to spec‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ify conditions for the use of particular tags.  For example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle -e '*:-command-:*' tag-order '[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         if [[ -n $PREFIX$SUFFIX ]]; then[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                           reply=( )[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         else[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                           reply=( - )[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         fi'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Completion  in command position will be attempted only if the string typed[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              so far is not empty.  This is tested using the PREFIX  special  parameter;[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              see  zshcompwid  for  a description of parameters which are special inside[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion widgets.  Setting reply to an empty array provides the  default[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              behaviour  of  trying  all tags at once; setting it to an array containing[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              only a hyphen disables the use of all tags and hence of all completions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If no tag-order  style  has  been  defined  for  a  context,  the  strings[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `(|*-)argument-* (|*-)option-* values' and `options' plus all tags offered[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              by  the completion function will be used to provide a sensible default be‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              havior that causes arguments (whether normal command  arguments  or  argu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ments of options) to be completed before option names for most commands.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       urls   This is used together with the urls tag by functions completing URLs.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the value consists of more than one string, or if the only string does[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              not name a file or directory, the strings are used as  the  URLs  to  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              plete.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the  value contains only one string which is the name of a normal file[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the URLs are taken from that file (where the  URLs  may  be  separated  by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              white space or newlines).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Finally,  if the only string in the value names a directory, the directory[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              hierarchy rooted at this directory gives the completions.  The  top  level[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              directory  should be the file access method, such as `http', `ftp', `book‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mark' and so on.  In many cases the next level of directories  will  be  a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              filename.  The directory hierarchy can descend as deep as necessary.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For example,[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' urls ~/.urls[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     mkdir -p ~/.urls/ftp/ftp.zsh.org/pub[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              allows  completion  of all the components of the URL ftp://ftp.zsh.org/pub[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              after suitable commands such as `netscape' or `lynx'.  Note, however, that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              access methods and files are completed separately, so if the  hosts  style[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is set hosts can be completed without reference to the urls style.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              See  the  description  in  the  function _urls itself for more information[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              (e.g. `more $^fpath/_urls(N)').[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       use-cache[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If this is set, the completion caching layer is activated for any  comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions  which use it (via the _store_cache, _retrieve_cache, and _cache_in‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              valid functions).  The directory containing the cache files can be changed[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with the cache-path style.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       use-compctl[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If this style is set to a string not equal to false, 0, no, and  off,  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion  system  may use any completion specifications defined with the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              compctl builtin command.  If the style is unset, this is done only if  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              zsh/compctl  module  is loaded.  The string may also contain the substring[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `first' to use completions defined with `compctl -T',  and  the  substring[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `default' to use the completion defined with `compctl -D'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note  that  this is only intended to smooth the transition from compctl to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the new completion system and may disappear in the future.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note also that the definitions from compctl will only be used if there  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              no specific completion function for the command in question.  For example,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              if there is a function _foo to complete arguments to the command foo, com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pctl  will never be invoked for foo.  However, the compctl version will be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tried if foo only uses default completion.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       use-ip By default, the function _hosts that completes host names  strips  IP  ad‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              dresses  from  entries read from host databases such as NIS and ssh files.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If this style is `true', the corresponding IP addresses can  be  completed[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              as  well.   This  style is not use in any context where the hosts style is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              set; note also it must be set before the cache of host names is  generated[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              (typically the first completion attempt).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       users  This  may be set to a list of usernames to be completed.  If it is not set[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              all usernames will be completed.  Note that if it is set only that list of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              users will be completed; this is because  on  some  systems  querying  all[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              users can take a prohibitive amount of time.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       users-hosts[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The values of this style should be of the form `user@host' or `user:host'.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              It  is  used  for  commands that need pairs of user- and hostnames.  These[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              commands will complete usernames from this style (only), and will restrict[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              subsequent hostname completion to hosts paired with that user  in  one  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the values of the style.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              It  is  possible to group values for sets of commands which allow a remote[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              login, such as rlogin and ssh, by using the my-accounts  tag.   Similarly,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              values  for  sets of commands which usually refer to the accounts of other[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              people, such as talk and finger, can be grouped  by  using  the  other-ac‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              counts tag.  More ambivalent commands may use the accounts tag.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       users-hosts-ports[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Like  users-hosts but used for commands like telnet and containing strings[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of the form `user@host:port'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       verbose[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If set, as it is by default, the completion listing is more  verbose.   In[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              particular  many  commands  show descriptions for options if this style is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `true'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       word   This is used by the _list completer, which prevents the insertion of  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pletions  until a second completion attempt when the line has not changed.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The normal way of finding out if the line has changed is  to  compare  its[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              entire  contents  between the two occasions.  If this style is `true', the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              comparison is instead performed only on the current word.  Hence  if  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pletion  is  performed  on another word with the same contents, completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will not be delayed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242mCONTROL FUNCTIONS[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       The initialization script compinit redefines all the widgets which  perform  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       pletion  to call the supplied widget function _main_complete.  This function acts[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       as a wrapper calling the so-called `completer' functions that  generate  matches.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       If  _main_complete is called with arguments, these are taken as the names of com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       pleter functions to be called in the order given.  If no arguments are given, the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       set of functions to try is taken from the completer style.  For example,  to  use[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       normal completion and correction if that doesn't generate any matches:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              zstyle ':completion:*' completer _complete _correct[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       after calling compinit. The default value for this style is `_complete _ignored',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       i.e. normally only ordinary completion is tried, first with the effect of the ig‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       nored-patterns  style  and then without it.  The _main_complete function uses the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       return status of the completer functions to decide if other completers should  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       called.   If  the  return  status  is zero, no other completers are tried and the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       _main_complete function returns.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       If the first argument to _main_complete is a single hyphen,  the  arguments  will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       not  be  taken as names of completers.  Instead, the second argument gives a name[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       to use in the completer field of the context and the other arguments give a  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       mand name and arguments to call to generate the matches.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The  following  completer  functions  are contained in the distribution, although[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       users may write their own.  Note that  in  contexts  the  leading  underscore  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       stripped,  for  example  basic  completion  is performed in the context `:comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tion::complete:...'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _all_matches[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This completer can be used  to  add  a  string  consisting  of  all  other[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matches.   As  it  influences later completers it must appear as the first[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completer in the list.  The  list  of  all  matches  is  affected  by  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              avoid-completer and old-matches styles described above.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              It  may  be  useful  to  use the _generic function described below to bind[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _all_matches to its own keystroke, for example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zle -C all-matches complete-word _generic[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     bindkey '^Xa' all-matches[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:all-matches:*' old-matches only[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:all-matches::::' completer _all_matches[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note that this does not generate completions by itself:  first use any  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  standard  ways  of  generating a list of completions, then use ^Xa to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              show all matches.  It is possible instead to add a standard  completer  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  list  and request that the list of all matches should be directly in‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              serted:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:all-matches::::' completer \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            _all_matches _complete[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:all-matches:*' insert true[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In this case the old-matches style should not be set.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _approximate[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is similar to the basic _complete completer but  allows  the  comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions  to undergo corrections.  The maximum number of errors can be speci‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fied by the max-errors style; see the description of approximate  matching[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in  zshexpn(1)  for  how errors are counted.  Normally this completer will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              only be tried after the normal _complete completer:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' completer _complete _approximate[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This will give correcting completion if  and  only  if  normal  completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              yields no possible completions.  When corrected completions are found, the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completer  will  normally  start  menu  completion  allowing  you to cycle[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              through these strings.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This completer uses the tags corrections and original when generating  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              possible  corrections  and  the original string.  The format style for the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              former may contain the additional sequences `%e' and `%o'  which  will  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              replaced  by the number of errors accepted to generate the corrections and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the original string, respectively.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The completer progressively increases the number of errors allowed  up  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the limit by the max-errors style, hence if a completion is found with one[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              error,  no completions with two errors will be shown, and so on.  It modi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fies the completer name in the context to indicate the  number  of  errors[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              being  tried:  on  the  first  try  the completer field contains `approxi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mate-1', on the second try `approximate-2', and so on.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              When _approximate is called from another function, the number of errors to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              accept may be passed with the -a option.  The argument is in the same for‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mat as the max-errors style, all in one string.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note that this completer (and the _correct completer mentioned below)  can[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be  quite  expensive to call, especially when a large number of errors are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              allowed.  One way to avoid this is to set up the completer style using the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              -e option to zstyle so that some completers are only used when  completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is attempted a second time on the same string, e.g.:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle -e ':completion:*' completer '[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       if [[ $_last_try != "$HISTNO$BUFFER$CURSOR" ]]; then[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         _last_try="$HISTNO$BUFFER$CURSOR"[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         reply=(_complete _match _prefix)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       else[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         reply=(_ignored _correct _approximate)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       fi'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This  uses  the HISTNO parameter and the BUFFER and CURSOR special parame‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ters that are available inside zle and completion widgets to find  out  if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  command line hasn't changed since the last time completion was tried.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Only then are the _ignored, _correct and _approximate completers called.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _canonical_paths [ -A var ] [ -N ] [ -MJV12nfX ] tag descr [ paths ... ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This completion function completes all paths given to it, and  also  tries[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to  offer  completions  which  point  to the same file as one of the paths[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              given (relative path when an absolute path is given, and vice versa;  when[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ..'s are present in the word to be completed; and some paths got from sym‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              links).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -A, if specified, takes the paths from the array variable specified. Paths[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              can  also  be specified on the command line as shown above.  -N, if speci‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fied, prevents canonicalizing the paths given before using them  for  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pletion,  in case they are already so. The options -M, -J, -V, -1, -2, -n,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              -F, -X are passed to compadd.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              See _description for a description of tag and descr.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _cmdambivalent[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Completes the remaining positional arguments as an external command.   The[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              external command and its arguments are completed as separate arguments (in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              a manner appropriate for completing /usr/bin/env) if there are two or more[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              remaining  positional  arguments on the command line, and as a quoted com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mand string (in the manner of system(...)) otherwise.  See also _cmdstring[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and _precommand.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This function takes no arguments.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _cmdstring[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Completes an external command as a single argument, as for system(...).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _complete[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This completer generates all possible completions in  a  context-sensitive[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              manner,  i.e.  using  the  settings  defined with the compdef function ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              plained above and the current settings of all  special  parameters.   This[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              gives the normal completion behaviour.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              To  complete  arguments  of  commands, _complete uses the utility function[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _normal, which is in turn responsible for finding the particular function;[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              it is described below.  Various contexts of the form -context- are handled[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              specifically. These are all mentioned above as possible arguments  to  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              #compdef tag.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Before  trying to find a function for a specific context, _complete checks[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              if the parameter `compcontext' is set. Setting  `compcontext'  allows  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              usual  completion  dispatching  to be overridden which is useful in places[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              such as a function that uses vared for input. If it is set  to  an  array,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  elements are taken to be the possible matches which will be completed[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              using the tag `values' and the description `value'. If it is set to an as‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sociative array, the keys are used as the  possible  completions  and  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              values (if non-empty) are used as descriptions for the matches.  If `comp‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              context'  is  set  to a string containing colons, it should be of the form[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `tag:descr:action'.  In this case the tag and descr give the tag  and  de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              scription  to use and the action indicates what should be completed in one[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of the forms accepted by the _arguments utility function described below.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Finally, if `compcontext' is set to a string without colons, the value  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              taken  as the name of the context to use and the function defined for that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              context will be called.  For this purpose,  there  is  a  special  context[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              named  -command-line-  that  completes  whole  command lines (commands and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              their arguments).  This is not used by the completion system itself but is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              nonetheless handled when explicitly called.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _correct[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Generate corrections, but not completions, for the current word;  this  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              similar  to _approximate but will not allow any number of extra characters[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              at  the  cursor  as  that  completer  does.   The  effect  is  similar  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              spell-checking.   It  is based on _approximate, but the completer field in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the context name is correct.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For example, with:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:::::' completer \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            _complete _correct _approximate[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:correct:::' max-errors 2 not-numeric[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:approximate:::' max-errors 3 numeric[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              correction will accept up to two errors.  If a numeric argument is  given,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              correction  will  not be performed, but correcting completion will be, and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will accept as many errors as given by the numeric  argument.   Without  a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              numeric  argument, first correction and then correcting completion will be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tried, with the first one accepting two errors and the second one  accept‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ing three errors.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              When  _correct is called as a function, the number of errors to accept may[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be given following the -a option.  The argument is in the same form a val‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ues to the accept style, all in one string.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This completer function is intended to be used  without  the  _approximate[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completer  or, as in the example, just before it.  Using it after the _ap‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              proximate completer is useless since _approximate will at  least  generate[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  corrected strings generated by the _correct completer -- and probably[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              more.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _expand[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This completer function does not really perform  completion,  but  instead[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              checks  if  the word on the command line is eligible for expansion and, if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              it is, gives detailed control over how this expansion is done.   For  this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to  happen,  the completion system needs to be invoked with complete-word,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              not expand-or-complete (the default binding for  TAB),  as  otherwise  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              string  will be expanded by the shell's internal mechanism before the com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pletion system is started.  Note also this completer should be called  be‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fore the _complete completer function.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The tags used when generating expansions are all-expansions for the string[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              containing  all  possible  expansions, expansions when adding the possible[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              expansions as single matches and original when adding the original  string[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              from the line.  The order in which these strings are generated, if at all,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              can be controlled by the group-order and tag-order styles, as usual.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  format  string  for all-expansions and for expansions may contain the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sequence `%o' which will be replaced by the original string from the line.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The kind of expansion to be tried is controlled by  the  substitute,  glob[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and subst-globs-only styles.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              It  is also possible to call _expand as a function, in which case the dif‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ferent modes may be selected with options: -s for substitute, -g for  glob[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and -o for subst-globs-only.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _expand_alias[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If the word the cursor is on is an alias, it is expanded and no other com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleters  are called.  The types of aliases which are to be expanded can be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              controlled with the styles regular, global and disabled.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This function is also a bindable command, see the section  `Bindable  Com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mands' below.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _extensions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the cursor follows the string `*.', filename extensions are completed.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The extensions are taken from files in current directory  or  a  directory[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              specified at the beginning of the current word. For exact matches, comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion  continues  to  allow  other completers such as _expand to expand the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pattern. The standard add-space and prefix-hidden styles are observed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _external_pwds[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Completes current directories of other zsh processes belonging to the cur‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rent user.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This is intended to be used via _generic, bound to a custom  key  combina‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion. Note that pattern matching is enabled so matching is performed simi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              lar to how it works with the _match completer.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _history[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Complete  words  from the shell's command  history.  This completer can be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              controlled by the remove-all-dups,  and  sort  styles  as  for  the  _his‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tory_complete_word  bindable  command, see the section `Bindable Commands'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              below and the section `Completion System Configuration' above.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _ignored[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The ignored-patterns style can be set to a list of patterns which are com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pared against possible completions; matching ones are removed.  With  this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completer those matches can be reinstated, as if no ignored-patterns style[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              were set.  The completer actually generates its own list of matches; which[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completers  are  invoked  is determined in the same way as for the _prefix[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completer.  The single-ignored style is also available as described above.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _list  This completer allows the insertion of matches to be delayed until comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion is attempted a second  time  without  the  word  on  the  line  being[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              changed.   On  the  first attempt, only the list of matches will be shown.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              It is affected by the styles condition and word, see the section  `Comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion System Configuration' above.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _match This  completer  is intended to be used after the _complete completer.  It[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              behaves similarly but the string on the command line may be a  pattern  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              match  against  trial completions.  This gives the effect of the GLOB_COM‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              PLETE option.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Normally completion will be performed by taking the pattern from the line,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              inserting a `*' at the cursor position and comparing the resulting pattern[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with the possible completions generated.  This can be  modified  with  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              match-original style described above.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  generated matches will be offered in a menu completion unless the in‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sert-unambiguous style is set to `true'; see  the  description  above  for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              other options for this style.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note  that  matcher specifications defined globally or used by the comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion functions (the styles matcher-list and matcher) will not be used.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _menu  This completer was written as simple example function  to  show  how  menu[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion  can  be enabled in shell code. However, it has the notable ef‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fect of disabling menu selection which can be useful with  _generic  based[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              widgets.  It should be used as the first completer in the list.  Note that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              this is independent of the setting of the MENU_COMPLETE  option  and  does[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              not  work with the other menu completion widgets such as reverse-menu-com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              plete, or accept-and-menu-complete.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _oldlist[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This completer controls how the standard completion  widgets  behave  when[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              there  is an existing list of completions which may have been generated by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              a special completion (i.e. a separately-bound completion command).  It al‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              lows the ordinary completion keys to continue to use the list  of  comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions  thus generated, instead of producing a new list of ordinary contex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tual completions.  It should appear in the list of completers  before  any[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of  the  widgets which generate matches.  It uses two styles: old-list and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              old-menu, see the section `Completion System Configuration' above.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _precommand[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Complete an external command in word-separated arguments, as for exec  and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              /usr/bin/env.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _prefix[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  completer  can be used to try completion with the suffix (everything[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              after the cursor) ignored.  In other words, the suffix will not be consid‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ered to be part of the word to complete.  The effect is similar to the ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pand-or-complete-prefix command.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The completer style is used to decide which other  completers  are  to  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              called  to  generate  matches.   If  this style is unset, the list of com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleters set for the current context is used  --  except,  of  course,  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _prefix  completer  itself.   Furthermore,  if this completer appears more[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              than once in the list of completers  only  those  completers  not  already[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tried by the last invocation of _prefix will be called.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For example, consider this global completer style:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' completer \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         _complete _prefix _correct _prefix:foo[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Here,  the _prefix completer tries normal completion but ignoring the suf‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fix.  If that doesn't generate any matches, and neither does the  call  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the _correct completer after it, _prefix will be called a second time and,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              now only trying correction with the suffix ignored.  On the second invoca‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion the completer part of the context appears as `foo'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              To  use  _prefix as the last resort and try only normal completion when it[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is invoked:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*' completer _complete ... _prefix[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion::prefix:*' completer _complete[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The add-space style is also respected.  If it is set to `true' then  _pre‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fix  will  insert  a  space between the matches generated (if any) and the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              suffix.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note that this completer is only useful if the COMPLETE_IN_WORD option  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              set;  otherwise,  the  cursor will be moved to the end of the current word[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              before the completion code is called and hence there will be no suffix.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _user_expand[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This completer behaves similarly to the _expand completer but instead per‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              forms expansions defined by users.  The styles add-space and  sort  styles[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              specific to the _expand completer are usable with _user_expand in addition[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to  other styles handled more generally by the completion system.  The tag[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              all-expansions is also available.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The expansion depends on the array style user-expand being defined for the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              current context; remember that the context for completers is less specific[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              than that for contextual completion as the full context has not  yet  been[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              determined.  Elements of the array may have one of the following forms:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              $hash[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     hash  is the name of an associative array.  Note this is not a full[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     parameter expression, merely a $, suitably quoted to prevent  imme‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     diate  expansion, followed by the name of an associative array.  If[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     the trial expansion word matches a key in hash, the  resulting  ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     pansion is the corresponding value.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _func[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _func  is the name of a shell function whose name must begin with _[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     but is not otherwise special to the completion system.   The  func‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     tion  is called with the trial word as an argument.  If the word is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     to be expanded, the function should set the array reply to  a  list[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     of expansions.  Optionally, it can set REPLY to a word that will be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     used as a description for the set of expansions.  The return status[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     of the function is irrelevant.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242mBINDABLE COMMANDS[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       In  addition to the context-dependent completions provided, which are expected to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       work in an intuitively obvious way, there are a few widgets implementing  special[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       behaviour  which  can  be  bound  separately to keys.  The following is a list of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       these and their default bindings.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _bash_completions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  is  used   by   two   widgets,   _bash_complete-word   and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _bash_list-choices.   It  exists  to provide compatibility with completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              bindings in bash.  The last character of the binding  determines  what  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completed:  `!',  command  names;  `$',  environment  variables; `@', host[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              names; `/', file names; `~' user names.  In bash, the binding preceded  by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `\e'  gives  completion,  and  preceded by `^X' lists options.  As some of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              these bindings clash with standard zsh bindings, only `\e~' and `^X~'  are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              bound  by  default.   To  add  the  rest, the following should be added to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              .zshrc after compinit has been run:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     for key in '!' '$' '@' '/' '~'; do[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       bindkey "\e$key" _bash_complete-word[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       bindkey "^X$key" _bash_list-choices[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     done[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This includes the bindings for `~' in case  they  were  already  bound  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              something else; the completion code does not override user bindings.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _correct_filename (^XC)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Correct the filename path at the cursor position.  Allows up to six errors[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in  the  name.   Can also be called with an argument to correct a filename[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              path, independently of zle; the correction is printed on standard output.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _correct_word (^Xc)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Performs correction of the current argument  using  the  usual  contextual[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completions  as possible choices. This stores the string `correct-word' in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the function field of the context name and then calls  the  _correct  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleter.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _expand_alias (^Xa)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  can  be used as a completer and as a bindable command.  It[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              expands the word the cursor is on if it is an alias.  The types  of  alias[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              expanded can be controlled with the styles regular, global and disabled.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              When  used  as a bindable command there is one additional feature that can[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be selected by setting the complete style to `true'.  In this case, if the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              word is not the name of an alias, _expand_alias tries to complete the word[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to a full alias name without expanding it.  It leaves the cursor  directly[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              after the completed word so that invoking _expand_alias once more will ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pand the now-complete alias name.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _expand_word (^Xe)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Performs  expansion  on  the current word:  equivalent to the standard ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pand-word command, but using the _expand completer.   Before  calling  it,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the function field of the context is set to `expand-word'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _generic[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  is not defined as a widget and not bound by default.  How‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ever, it can be used to define a widget and will then store  the  name  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  widget  in  the function field of the context and call the completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              system.  This allows custom completion widgets with their own set of style[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              settings to be defined easily.  For example, to define a widget that  per‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              forms normal completion and starts menu selection:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zle -C foo complete-word _generic[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     bindkey '...' foo[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:foo:*' menu yes select=1[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note  in particular that the completer style may be set for the context in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              order to change the set of functions used to  generate  possible  matches.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  _generic  is  called  with  arguments,  those  are  passed  through to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _main_complete as the list of completers in place of those defined by  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completer style.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _history_complete_word (\e/)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Complete  words  from the shell's command history. This uses the list, re‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              move-all-dups, sort, and stop styles.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _most_recent_file (^Xm)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Complete the name of the most recently modified file matching the  pattern[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              on  the command line (which may be blank).  If given a numeric argument N,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              complete the Nth most recently modified file.   Note  the  completion,  if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              any, is always unique.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _next_tags (^Xn)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  command  alters the set of matches used to that for the next tag, or[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              set of tags, either as given by the tag-order style or as set by  default;[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              these matches would otherwise not be available.  Successive invocations of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the command cycle through all possible sets of tags.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _read_comp (^X^R)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Prompt  the  user  for a string, and use that to perform completion on the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              current word.  There are two possibilities for the string.  First, it  can[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be  a  set  of words beginning `_', for example `_files -/', in which case[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the function with any arguments will be called  to  generate  the  comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions.  Unambiguous parts of the function name will be completed automati‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cally  (normal completion is not available at this point) until a space is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              typed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Second, any other string will be passed as a set of arguments  to  compadd[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and should hence be an expression specifying what should be completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              A  very  restricted  set of editing commands is available when reading the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              string:  `DEL' and `^H' delete the last character; `^U' deletes the  line,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and  `^C' and `^G' abort the function, while `RET' accepts the completion.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Note the string is used verbatim as a command line, so arguments  must  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              quoted in accordance with standard shell rules.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Once  a string has been read, the next call to _read_comp will use the ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              isting string instead of reading a new one.  To force a new string  to  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              read, call _read_comp with a numeric argument.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _complete_debug (^X?)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This widget performs ordinary completion, but captures in a temporary file[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              a  trace  of  the  shell commands executed by the completion system.  Each[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion attempt gets its own file.  A command to  view  each  of  these[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              files is pushed onto the editor buffer stack.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _complete_help (^Xh)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  widget  displays  information about the context names, the tags, and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the completion functions used when completing at the current cursor  posi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion.  If  given a numeric argument other than 1 (as in `ESC-2 ^Xh'), then[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the styles used and the contexts for which they are used  will  be  shown,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              too.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note  that  the  information about styles may be incomplete; it depends on[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the information available from the completion functions called,  which  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              turn is determined by the user's own styles and other settings.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _complete_help_generic[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Unlike  other  commands  listed here, this must be created as a normal ZLE[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              widget rather than a completion widget (i.e. with zle -N).  It is used for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              generating help with a widget bound to the _generic  widget  that  is  de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              scribed above.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  this widget is created using the name of the function, as it is by de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fault, then when executed it will read a key sequence.  This  is  expected[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to be bound to a call to a completion function that uses the _generic wid‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              get.   That  widget will be executed, and information provided in the same[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              format that the _complete_help widget displays for contextual completion.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the widget's name contains debug, for example if it is created as  `zle[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              -N  _complete_debug_generic _complete_help_generic', it will read and exe‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cute the keystring for a generic widget as before, but then  generate  de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              bugging information as done by _complete_debug for contextual completion.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the widget's name contains noread, it will not read a keystring but in‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              stead  arrange that the next use of a generic widget run in the same shell[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will have the effect as described above.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The widget works by setting the shell  parameter  ZSH_TRACE_GENERIC_WIDGET[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              which  is  read  by _generic.  Unsetting the parameter cancels any pending[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              effect of the noread form.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For example, after executing the following:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zle -N _complete_debug_generic _complete_help_generic[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     bindkey '^x:' _complete_debug_generic[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              typing `C-x :' followed by the key sequence  for  a  generic  widget  will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cause trace output for that widget to be saved to a file.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _complete_tag (^Xt)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This widget completes symbol tags created by the etags or ctags programmes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              (note  there is no connection with the completion system's tags) stored in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              a file TAGS, in the format used by etags, or tags, in the  format  created[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              by  ctags.   It  will look back up the path hierarchy for the first occur‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rence of either file; if both exist, the file TAGS is preferred.  You  can[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              specify  the  full  path  to  a TAGS or tags file by setting the parameter[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              $TAGSFILE or $tagsfile respectively.  The  corresponding  completion  tags[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used are etags and vtags, after emacs and vi respectively.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242mUTILITY FUNCTIONS[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       Descriptions follow for utility functions that may be useful when writing comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       tion  functions.  If functions are installed in subdirectories, most of these re‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       side in the Base subdirectory.  Like the example functions for  commands  in  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       distribution,  the utility functions generating matches all follow the convention[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       of returning status zero if they generated completions and non-zero if no  match‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       ing completions could be added.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _absolute_command_paths[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function completes external commands as absolute paths (unlike _com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mand_names -e which completes their basenames).  It takes no arguments.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _all_labels [ -x ] [ -12VJ ] tag name descr [ command arg ... ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is a convenient interface to the _next_label function  below,  imple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              menting  the  loop  shown in the _next_label example.  The command and its[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              arguments are called to generate the matches.  The options stored  in  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              parameter  name will automatically be inserted into the args passed to the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              command.  Normally, they are put directly after the command, but if one of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the args is a single hyphen, they are inserted directly before  that.   If[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the hyphen is the last argument, it will be removed from the argument list[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              before  the  command is called.  This allows _all_labels to be used in al‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              most all cases where the matches can be generated by a single call to  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              compadd builtin command or by a call to one of the utility functions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     local expl[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     if _requested foo; then[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       _all_labels foo expl '...' compadd ... - $matches[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     fi[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Will  complete  the strings from the matches parameter, using compadd with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              additional options which will take  precedence  over  those  generated  by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _all_labels.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _alternative [ -O name ] [ -C name ] spec ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This function is useful in simple cases where multiple tags are available.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Essentially  it  implements  a  loop  like the one described for the _tags[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function below.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The tags to use and the action to perform if a tag is  requested  are  de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              scribed  using  the  specs which are of the form: `tag:descr:action'.  The[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tags are offered using _tags and if the tag is requested,  the  action  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              executed with the given description descr.  The actions are those accepted[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              by  the  _arguments  function (described below), with the following excep‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions:[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              •      The `->state' and `=...' forms are not supported.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              •      The `((a\:bar b\:baz))' form does not need the colon to be escaped,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     since the specs have no colon-separated fields after the action.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For example, the action may be a simple function call:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _alternative \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         'users:user:_users' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         'hosts:host:_hosts'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              offers usernames and hostnames  as  possible  matches,  generated  by  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _users and _hosts functions respectively.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Like  _arguments,  this  function uses _all_labels to execute the actions,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              which will loop over all sets of tags.  Special handling is only  required[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              if  there is an additional valid tag, for example inside a function called[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              from _alternative.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The option `-O name' is used in the same way as by  the  _arguments  func‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion.   In  other  words, the elements of the name array will be passed to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              compadd when executing an action.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Like _tags this function supports the -C option to give a  different  name[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for the argument context field.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _arguments [ -nswWCRS ] [ -A pat ] [ -O name ] [ -M matchspec ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                  [ : ] spec ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       _arguments [ opt ... ] -- [ -l ] [ -i pats ] [ -s pair ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                  [ helpspec ...][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function can be used to give a complete specification for completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for a command whose arguments follow standard  UNIX  option  and  argument[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              conventions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Options Overview[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Options  to  _arguments  itself must be in separate words, i.e. -s -w, not[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              -sw.  The options are followed by specs that describe  options  and  argu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ments  of the analyzed command.  To avoid ambiguity, all options to _argu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ments itself may be separated from the spec forms by a single colon.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The `--' form is used to intuit spec forms from the  help  output  of  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              command  being  analyzed,  and is described in detail below.  The opts for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the `--' form are otherwise the same options as the first form.  Note that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `-s' following `--' has a distinct meaning from `-s' preceding  `--',  and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              both may appear.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  option  switches  -s, -S, -A, -w, and -W affect how _arguments parses[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the analyzed command line's options.  These switches are useful  for  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mands with standard argument parsing.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The options of _arguments have the following meanings:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -n     With  this option, _arguments sets the parameter NORMARG to the po‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     sition of the first normal argument in the $words array,  i.e.  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     position  after  the  end of the options.  If that argument has not[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     been reached, NORMARG is set to -1.  The caller should declare `in‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     teger NORMARG' if the -n option is passed; otherwise the  parameter[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     is not used.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -s     Enable  option stacking for single-letter options, whereby multiple[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     single-letter options may be combined into a single word.  For  ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     ample,  the two options `-x' and `-y' may be combined into a single[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     word `-xy'.  By default, every word corresponds to a single  option[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     name (`-xy' is a single option named `xy').[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     Options  beginning  with  a single hyphen or plus sign are eligible[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     for stacking; words beginning with two hyphens are not.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     Note that -s after -- has a different meaning, which is  documented[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     in the segment entitled `Deriving spec forms from the help output'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -w     In  combination  with -s, allow option stacking even if one or more[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     of the options take arguments.  For example, if -x takes  an  argu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     ment,  with  no -s, `-xy' is considered as a single (unhandled) op‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     tion; with -s, -xy is an option with the argument `y'; with both -s[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     and -w, -xy is the option -x and the option -y with arguments to -x[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     (and to -y, if it takes arguments)  still  to  come  in  subsequent[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     words.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -W     This  option  takes -w a stage further:  it is possible to complete[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     single-letter options even after an argument  that  occurs  in  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     same word.  However, it depends on the action performed whether op‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     tions  will  really  be completed at this point.  For more control,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     use a utility function like _guard as part of the action.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -C     Modify  the  curcontext  parameter  for  an  action  of  the   form[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     `->state'.  This is discussed in detail below.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -R     Return  status  300 instead of zero when a $state is to be handled,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     in the `->string' syntax.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -S     Do not complete options after a `--' appearing on the line, and ig‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     nore the `--'.  For example, with -S, in the line[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                            foobar -x -- -y[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     the `-x' is considered an option, the `-y' is considered  an  argu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     ment, and the `--' is considered to be neither.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -A pat Do  not complete options after the first non-option argument on the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     line.  pat is a pattern matching all strings which are  not  to  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     taken  as arguments.  For example, to make _arguments stop complet‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     ing options after the  first  normal  argument,  but  ignoring  all[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     strings  starting  with  a hyphen even if they are not described by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     one of the optspecs, the form is `-A "-*"'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -O name[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     Pass the elements of the  array  name  as  arguments  to  functions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     called to execute actions.  This is discussed in detail below.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -M matchspec[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     Use  the  match specification matchspec for completing option names[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     and values.  The default matchspec allows partial  word  completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     after  `_'  and  `-', such as completing `-f-b' to `-foo-bar'.  The[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     default matchspec is:[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     r:|[_-]=* r:|=*[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -0     When populating values of the `opt_args' associative  array,  don't[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     backslash-escape  colons  and  backslashes  and use NUL rather than[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     colon for joining multiple values. This option is described in more[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     detail below, under the heading specs: actions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              specs: overview[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Each of the following forms is a spec describing individual  sets  of  op‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions or arguments on the command line being analyzed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              n:message:action[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              n::message:action[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     This  describes  the  n'th  normal  argument.   The message will be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     printed above the matches generated and the action  indicates  what[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     can  be  completed  in this position (see below).  If there are two[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     colons before the message the argument is optional.  If the message[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     contains only white  space,  nothing  will  be  printed  above  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     matches unless the action adds an explanation string itself.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              :message:action[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ::message:action[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     Similar, but describes the next argument, whatever number that hap‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     pens  to  be.   If  all arguments are specified in this form in the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     correct order the numbers are unnecessary.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              *:message:action[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              *::message:action[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              *:::message:action[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     This describes how arguments (usually non-option  arguments,  those[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     not  beginning with - or +) are to be completed when neither of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     first two forms was provided.  Any number of arguments can be  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     pleted in this fashion.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     With two colons before the message, the words special array and the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     CURRENT  special parameter are modified to refer only to the normal[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     arguments when the action is executed  or  evaluated.   With  three[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     colons  before  the  message they are modified to refer only to the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     normal arguments covered by this description.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              optspec[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              optspec:...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     This describes an option.  The colon indicates handling for one  or[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     more  arguments  to the option; if it is not present, the option is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     assumed to take no arguments.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     The following forms are available for the initial optspec,  whether[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     or not the option has arguments.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     *optspec[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            Here  optspec is one of the remaining forms below.  This in‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            dicates the following optspec may be repeated.  Otherwise if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            the corresponding option is already present on  the  command[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            line to the left of the cursor it will not be offered again.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     -optname[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     +optname[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            In the simplest form the optspec is just the option name be‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            ginning  with  a  minus or a plus sign, such as `-foo'.  The[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            first argument for the option (if any) must follow as a sep‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            arate word directly after the option.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                            Either of `-+optname' and `+-optname' can be used to specify[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            that -optname and +optname are both valid.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                            In all the remaining forms, the leading `-' may be  replaced[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            by or paired with `+' in this way.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     -optname-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            The  first  argument  of the option must come directly after[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            the option name in the same word.  For example,  `-foo-:...'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            specifies  that  the completed option and argument will look[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            like `-fooarg'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     -optname+[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            The first argument may appear immediately after  optname  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            the  same  word,  or may appear as a separate word after the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            option.  For example, `-foo+:...' specifies  that  the  com‐[0m
