[38;2;248;248;242m                            pleted  option  and argument will look like either `-fooarg'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            or `-foo arg'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     -optname=[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            The argument may appear as the next word, or in same word as[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            the option name provided that it is separated from it by  an[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            equals sign, for example `-foo=arg' or `-foo arg'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     -optname=-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            The  argument to the option must appear after an equals sign[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            in the same word, and may not be given in the next argument.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     optspec[explanation][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            An explanation string may be appended to any of the  preced‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            ing  forms  of  optspec  by  enclosing it in brackets, as in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            `-q[query operation]'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                            The verbose style is used to decide whether the  explanation[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            strings  are displayed with the option in a completion list‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            ing.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                            If no bracketed explanation string is given but the auto-de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            scription style is set and only one  argument  is  described[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            for  this optspec, the value of the style is displayed, with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            any appearance of the sequence `%d' in it  replaced  by  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            message  of  the  first optarg that follows the optspec; see[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            below.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     It is possible for options with a literal `+' or `=' to appear, but[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     that character must be quoted, for example `-\+'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     Each optarg following an optspec must take  one  of  the  following[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     forms:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     :message:action[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     ::message:action[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            An argument to the option; message and action are treated as[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            for  ordinary arguments.  In the first form, the argument is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            mandatory, and in the second form it is optional.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                            This group may be repeated for options which  take  multiple[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            arguments.   In  other words, :message1:action1:message2:ac‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            tion2 specifies that the option takes two arguments.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     :*pattern:message:action[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     :*pattern::message:action[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     :*pattern:::message:action[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            This describes multiple arguments.  Only the last optarg for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            an option taking multiple arguments may  be  given  in  this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            form.  If the pattern is empty (i.e. :*:), all the remaining[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            words  on  the  line are to be completed as described by the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            action; otherwise, all the words up to and including a  word[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            matching the pattern are to be completed using the action.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                            Multiple colons are treated as for the `*:...' forms for or‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            dinary  arguments:   when  the  message  is  preceded by two[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            colons, the words special array and the CURRENT special  pa‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            rameter  are  modified during the execution or evaluation of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            the action to refer only to  the  words  after  the  option.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            When  preceded  by  three colons, they are modified to refer[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            only to the words covered by this description.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Any literal colon in an optname, message, or action must be preceded by  a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              backslash, `\:'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Each of the forms above may be preceded by a list in parentheses of option[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              names  and  argument numbers.  If the given option is on the command line,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the options and arguments indicated in parentheses will  not  be  offered.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              For  example,  `(-two  -three  1)-one:...' completes the option `-one'; if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              this appears on the command line, the options  -two  and  -three  and  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              first  ordinary  argument  will  not  be completed after it.  `(-foo):...'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              specifies an ordinary argument completion; -foo will not be  completed  if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              that argument is already present.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Other items may appear in the list of excluded options to indicate various[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              other  items  that should not be applied when the current specification is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matched: a single star (*) for the rest arguments (i.e. a specification of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the form `*:...'); a colon (:) for all normal (non-option-) arguments; and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              a hyphen (-) for all options.  For example, if `(*)' appears before an op‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion and the option appears on the command line, the list of remaining ar‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              guments (those shown in the above table beginning with `*:') will  not  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              To  aid  in  reuse of specifications, it is possible to precede any of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              forms above with `!'; then the form will no longer be completed,  although[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              if the option or argument appears on the command line they will be skipped[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              as  normal.   The  main use for this is when the arguments are given by an[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              array, and _arguments is called repeatedly for more specific contexts:  on[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  first  call  `_arguments  $global_options' is used, and on subsequent[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              calls `_arguments !$^global_options'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              specs: actions[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In each of the forms above the action determines how completions should be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              generated.  Except for the `->string' form below, the action will be  exe‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cuted  by  calling the _all_labels function to process all tag labels.  No[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              special handling of tags is needed unless a function call introduces a new[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              one.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The functions called to execute actions will be called with  the  elements[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of  the  array  named  by  the `-O name' option as arguments.  This can be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used, for example, to pass the same set of options for the compadd builtin[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to all actions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The forms for action are as follows.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m               (single unquoted space)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     This is useful where an argument is required but it is not possible[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     or desirable to generate matches for it.  The message will be  dis‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     played  but no completions listed.  Note that even in this case the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     colon at the end of the message is needed; it may only  be  omitted[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     when neither a message nor an action is given.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              (item1 item2 ...)[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     One of a list of possible matches, for example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                            :foo:(foo bar baz)[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              ((item1\:desc1 ...))[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     Similar  to  the  above,  but  with  descriptions for each possible[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     match.  Note the backslash before the colon.  For example,[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                            :foo:((a\:bar b\:baz))[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     The matches will be listed together with their descriptions if  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     description style is set with the values tag in the context.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              ->string[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     In  this  form,  _arguments processes the arguments and options and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     then returns control to the calling function with parameters set to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     indicate the state of processing; the calling function  then  makes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     its  own  arrangements  for  generating  completions.  For example,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     functions that implement a state machine can use this type  of  ac‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     tion.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     Where  _arguments  encounters  action  in the `->string' format, it[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     will strip all leading and trailing whitespace from string and  set[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     the array state to the set of all strings for which an action is to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     be  performed.   The elements of the array state_descr are assigned[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     the corresponding message field from each optarg containing such an[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     action.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     By default and in common with all  other  well  behaved  completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     functions,  _arguments  returns  status  zero if it was able to add[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     matches and non-zero otherwise. However, if the -R option is given,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     _arguments will instead return a status of  300  to  indicate  that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     $state is to be handled.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     In  addition  to  $state and $state_descr, _arguments also sets the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     global parameters `context', `line' and `opt_args' as described be‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     low, and does not reset any changes made to the special  parameters[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     such  as  PREFIX  and  words.   This gives the calling function the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     choice of resetting these  parameters  or  propagating  changes  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     them.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     A function calling _arguments with at least one action containing a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     `->string' must therefore declare appropriate local parameters:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                            local context state state_descr line[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                            typeset -A opt_args[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     to prevent _arguments from altering the global environment.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              {eval-string}[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     A  string in braces is evaluated as shell code to generate matches.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     If the eval-string itself does not begin with an opening  parenthe‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     sis or brace it is split into separate words before execution.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              = action[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     If  the  action  starts  with  `=  '  (an equals sign followed by a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     space), _arguments will insert the contents of the  argument  field[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     of  the  current context as the new first element in the words spe‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     cial array and increment the value of the CURRENT  special  parame‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     ter.   This  has the effect of inserting a dummy word onto the com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     pletion command line while not changing the point at which  comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     tion is taking place.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     This  is  most  useful with one of the specifiers that restrict the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     words on the command line on which the action is  to  operate  (the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     two-  and  three-colon forms above).  One particular use is when an[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     action itself causes _arguments on a restricted range; it is neces‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     sary to use this trick to insert an appropriate command  name  into[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     the range for the second call to _arguments to be able to parse the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     line.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m               word...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              word...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     This covers all forms other than those above.  If the action starts[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     with  a  space,  the  remaining  list  of words will be invoked un‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     changed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     Otherwise it will be invoked with some extra strings  placed  after[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     the  first word; these are to be passed down as options to the com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     padd builtin.  They ensure that the state specified by  _arguments,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     in  particular  the  descriptions of options and arguments, is cor‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     rectly passed to the completion command.   These  additional  argu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     ments  are  taken from the array parameter `expl'; this will be set[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     up before executing the action and hence may be referred to  inside[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     it,  typically  in  an  expansion of the form `$expl[@]' which pre‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     serves empty elements of the array.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              During the performance of the action the array `line' will be set  to  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              normal  arguments  from  the command line, i.e. the words from the command[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              line after the command name excluding all  options  and  their  arguments.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Options  are  stored in the associative array `opt_args' with option names[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              as keys and their arguments as the values.  By  default,  all  colons  and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              backslashes  in  the  value are escaped with backslashes, and if an option[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              has multiple arguments (for example, when using an  optspec  of  the  form[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `*optspec'),  they are joined with (unescaped) colons.  However, if the -0[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              option was passed, no backslash escaping is performed, and multiple values[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              are joined with NUL bytes.  For example, after `zsh -o foo:foo -o  bar:bar[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              -o <TAB>', the contents of `opt_args' would be[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     typeset -A opt_args=( [-o]='foo\:foo:bar\:bar:' )[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              by default, and[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     typeset -A opt_args=( [-o]=$'foo:foo\x00bar:bar\x00' )[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              if _arguments had been called with the -0 option.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  parameter  `context' is set when returning to the calling function to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              perform an action of the form `->string'.  It is set to an array  of  ele‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ments corresponding to the elements of $state.  Each element is a suitable[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              name  for  the  argument field of the context: either a string of the form[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `option-opt-n' for the n'th argument of the option -opt, or  a  string  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  form  `argument-n' for the n'th argument.  For `rest' arguments, that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is those in the list at the end not handled by position, n is  the  string[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `rest'.   For  example, when completing the argument of the -o option, the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              name is `option-o-1', while for the second normal  (non-option-)  argument[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              it is `argument-2'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Furthermore,  during  the evaluation of the action the context name in the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              curcontext parameter is altered to append the same string that  is  stored[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in the context parameter.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  option  -C tells _arguments to modify the curcontext parameter for an[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              action of the form `->state'.  This is the standard parameter used to keep[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              track of the current context.  Here it (and not the context array)  should[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be  made  local to the calling function to avoid passing back the modified[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              value and should be initialised to the current value at the start  of  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     local curcontext="$curcontext"[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is  useful  where it is not possible for multiple states to be valid[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              together.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Grouping Options[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Options can be grouped to simplify exclusion lists. A group is  introduced[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with  `+'  followed  by a name for the group in the subsequent word. Whole[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              groups can then be referenced in an exclusion list or a group name can  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              used to disambiguate between two forms of the same option. For example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _arguments \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         '(group2--x)-a' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       + group1 \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         -m \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         '(group2)-n' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       + group2 \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         -x -y[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the  name  of  a group is specified in the form `(name)' then only one[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              value from that group will ever be completed; more formally, all  specifi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cations  are mutually exclusive to all other specifications in that group.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is useful for defining options that are aliases for each  other.  For[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _arguments \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         -a -b \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       + '(operation)' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         {-c,--compress}'[compress]' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         {-d,--decompress}'[decompress]' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         {-l,--list}'[list]'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  an  option in a group appears on the command line, it is stored in the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              associative array `opt_args' with 'group-option' as a key.  In the example[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              above, a key `operation--c' is used if the option `-c' is present  on  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              command line.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Specifying Multiple Sets of Arguments[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              It  is possible to specify multiple sets of options and arguments with the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sets separated by single hyphens. This differs from groups  in  that  sets[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              are considered to be mutually exclusive of each other.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Specifications  before  the first set and from any group are common to all[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sets. For example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _arguments \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         -a \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       - set1 \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         -c \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       - set2 \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         -d \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         ':arg:(x2 y2)'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This defines two sets.  When the command line contains  the  option  `-c',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  `-d'  option and the argument will not be considered possible comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions.  When it contains `-d' or an argument, the option `-c' will not  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              considered.  However, after `-a' both sets will still be considered valid.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              As  for  groups,  the  name of a set may appear in exclusion lists, either[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              alone or preceding a normal option or argument specification.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The completion code has to parse the command line separately for each set.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This can be slow so sets should only be used when necessary.  A useful al‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ternative is often an option  specification  with  rest-arguments  (as  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `-foo:*:...'); here the option -foo swallows up all remaining arguments as[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              described by the optarg definitions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Deriving spec forms from the help output[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  option  `--'  allows _arguments to work out the names of long options[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              that support the `--help' option which is standard in many  GNU  commands.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The command word is called with the argument `--help' and the output exam‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ined  for option names.  Clearly, it can be dangerous to pass this to com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mands which may not support this option as the behaviour of the command is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              unspecified.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In addition to options, `_arguments --' will try to deduce  the  types  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              arguments available for options when the form `--opt=val' is valid.  It is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              also  possible  to provide hints by examining the help text of the command[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and adding helpspec of the form `pattern:message:action'; note that  other[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _arguments  spec  forms  are not used.  The pattern is matched against the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              help text for an option, and if it matches the message and action are used[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              as for other argument specifiers.  The special case  of  `*:'  means  both[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              message and action are empty, which has the effect of causing options hav‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ing  no  description in the help output to be ordered in listings ahead of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              options that have a description.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _arguments -- '*\*:toggle:(yes no)' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                                   '*=FILE*:file:_files' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                                   '*=DIR*:directory:_files -/' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                                   '*=PATH*:directory:_files -/'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Here, `yes' and `no' will be completed as the argument  of  options  whose[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              description  ends in a star; file names will be completed for options that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              contain the substring `=FILE' in the description; and directories will  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completed  for  options whose description contains `=DIR' or `=PATH'.  The[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              last three are in fact the default and so need not  be  given  explicitly,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              although  it is possible to override the use of these patterns.  A typical[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              help text which uses this feature is:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                       -C, --directory=DIR          change to directory DIR[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              so that the above specifications will cause directories  to  be  completed[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              after `--directory', though not after `-C'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note  also that _arguments tries to find out automatically if the argument[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for an option is optional.  This can be specified explicitly  by  doubling[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the colon before the message.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the  pattern  ends in `(-)', this will be removed from the pattern and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the action will be used only directly after the `=', not in the next word.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is the behaviour of a normal  specification  defined  with  the  form[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `=-'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              By  default, the command (with the option `--help') is run after resetting[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              all the locale categories (except for LC_CTYPE) to `C'.  If the  localized[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              help  output  is known to work, the option `-l' can be specified after the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `_arguments --' so that the command is run in the current locale.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The `_arguments --' can be followed by the option `-i  patterns'  to  give[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              patterns  for  options which are not to be completed.  The patterns can be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              given as the name of an array parameter or as a literal list in  parenthe‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ses.  For example,[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _arguments -- -i \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         "(--(en|dis)able-FEATURE*)"[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              will cause completion to ignore the options `--enable-FEATURE' and `--dis‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              able-FEATURE' (this example is useful with GNU configure).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  `_arguments  --' form can also be followed by the option `-s pair' to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              describe option aliases.  The pair consists of a list of alternating  pat‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              terns  and  corresponding  replacements,  enclosed in parens and quoted so[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              that it forms a single argument word in the _arguments call.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For example, some configure-script help output describes options  only  as[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `--enable-foo',  but  the  script  also  accepts  the negated form `--dis‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              able-foo'.  To allow completion of the second form:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _arguments -- -s "((#s)--enable- --disable-)"[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Miscellaneous notes[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Finally, note that _arguments generally expects to be the primary function[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              handling any completion for which it is used.  It may  have  side  effects[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              which  change the treatment of any matches added by other functions called[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              after it.  To combine _arguments with  other  functions,  those  functions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              should  be called either before _arguments, as an action within a spec, or[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in handlers for `->state' actions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Here is a more general example of the use of _arguments:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _arguments '-l+:left border:' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                                '-format:paper size:(letter A4)' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                                '*-copy:output file:_files::resolution:(300 600)' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                                ':postscript file:_files -g \*.\(ps\|eps\)' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                                '*:page number:'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This describes three options: `-l', `-format',  and  `-copy'.   The  first[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              takes one argument described as `left border' for which no completion will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be  offered  because  of the empty action.  Its argument may come directly[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              after the `-l' or it may be given as the next word on the line.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The `-format' option takes one argument in the  next  word,  described  as[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `paper  size'  for  which  only the strings `letter' and `A4' will be com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleted.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The `-copy' option may appear more than once on the command line and takes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              two arguments.  The first is mandatory and will be completed  as  a  file‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              name.   The second is optional (because of the second colon before the de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              scription `resolution') and will be completed from the strings  `300'  and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `600'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  last two descriptions say what should be completed as arguments.  The[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              first describes the first argument as a `postscript file' and makes  files[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ending  in  `ps'  or  `eps'  be completed.  The last description gives all[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              other arguments the description `page number' but does not  offer  comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _cache_invalid cache_identifier[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  returns status zero if the completions cache corresponding[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to the given cache identifier needs rebuilding.   It  determines  this  by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              looking  up  the  cache-policy style for the current context.  This should[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              provide a function name which is run with the full path  to  the  relevant[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cache file as the only argument.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _example_caching_policy () {[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         # rebuild if cache is more than a week old[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         local -a oldp[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         oldp=( "$1"(Nm+7) )[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         (( $#oldp ))[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     }[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _call_function return name [ arg ... ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  a function name exists, it is called with the arguments args.  The re‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              turn argument gives the name of a parameter in  which  the  return  status[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              from  the  function  name should be stored; if return is empty or a single[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              hyphen it is ignored.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The return status of _call_function itself is zero if  the  function  name[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              exists and was called and non-zero otherwise.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _call_program [ -l ] [ -p ] tag string ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function provides a mechanism for the user to override the use of an[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              external command.  It looks up the command style with  the  supplied  tag.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the  style  is  set, its value is used as the command to execute.  The[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              strings from the call to _call_program, or from the style if set, are con‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              catenated with spaces between them and the resulting string is  evaluated.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The return status is the return status of the command called.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              By default, the command is run in an environment where all the locale cat‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              egories  (except  for  LC_CTYPE)  are  reset to `C' by calling the utility[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function _comp_locale (see below). If the option `-l' is given,  the  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mand is run with the current locale.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the option `-p' is supplied it indicates that the command output is in‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fluenced  by  the permissions it is run with. If the gain-privileges style[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is set to true, _call_program will make use of commands such as  sudo,  if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              present  on the command-line, to match the permissions to whatever the fi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              nal command is likely to run under. When looking  up  the  gain-privileges[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and  command  styles, the command component of the zstyle context will end[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with a slash (`/') followed by the command that  would  be  used  to  gain[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              privileges.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _combination [ -s pattern ] tag style spec ... field opts ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  is  used  to complete combinations of values,  for example[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pairs of hostnames and usernames.  The  style  argument  gives  the  style[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              which  defines the pairs; it is looked up in a context with the tag speci‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fied.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The style name consists of field names separated by hyphens,  for  example[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `users-hosts-ports'.   For each field for a value is already known, a spec[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of the form `field=pattern' is given.  For example, if the command line so[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              far specifies a user `pws', the argument `users=pws' should appear.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The next argument with no equals sign is taken as the name  of  the  field[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for  which  completions  should  be  generated  (presumably not one of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fields for which the value is known).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The matches generated will be taken from the value of  the  style.   These[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              should contain the possible values for the combinations in the appropriate[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              order (users, hosts, ports in the example above).  The values for the dif‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ferent  fields  are separated by colons.  This can be altered with the op‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion -s to _combination which specifies a pattern.  Typically  this  is  a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              character class, as for example `-s "[:@]"' in the case of the users-hosts[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              style.     Each  `field=pattern'  specification  restricts the completions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              which apply to elements of the style with appropriately matching fields.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If no style with the given name is defined for the given tag, or  if  none[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of the strings in style's value match, but a function name of the required[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              field  preceded  by an underscore is defined, that function will be called[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to generate the matches.  For example, if there is no  `users-hosts-ports'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              or  no  matching  hostname  when a host is required, the function `_hosts'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will automatically be called.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the same name is used for more than one field, in both the  `field=pat‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tern'  and  the argument that gives the name of the field to be completed,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the number of the field (starting with one) may be given after the  field‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              name, separated from it by a colon.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              All  arguments  after  the  required field name are passed to compadd when[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              generating matches from the style value,  or  to  the  functions  for  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fields if they are called.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _command_names [ -e | - ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This function completes words that are valid at command position: names of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              aliases,  builtins,  hashed  commands,  functions, and so on.  With the -e[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              flag, only hashed commands are completed.  The - flag is ignored.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _comp_locale[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This function resets all the locale categories other than LC_CTYPE to  `C'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              so  that  the  output from external commands can be easily analyzed by the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion system. LC_CTYPE retains the current value (taking  LC_ALL  and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              LANG  into  account), ensuring that non-ASCII characters in file names are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              still handled properly.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This function should normally be run only in a subshell, because  the  new[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              locale is exported to the environment. Typical usage would be `$(_comp_lo‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cale; command ...)'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _completers [ -p ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This function completes names of completers.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -p     Include the leading underscore (`_') in the matches.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _default[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  corresponds  to the -default- special context which is ap‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              plied where no completion is defined.  It is useful to call it under  cer‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tain error conditions such as completion after an unrecognised subcommand.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This applies the concept of graceful degradation to the completion system,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              allowing it to fallback on basic completion of commonly useful things like[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              filenames.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _describe [-12JVx] [ -oO | -t tag ] descr name1 [ name2 ] [ opt ... ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                 [ -- name1 [ name2 ] [ opt ... ] ... ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  associates completions with descriptions.  Multiple groups[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              separated by -- can be supplied, potentially with different completion op‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions opts.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The descr is taken as a string to display above the matches if the  format[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              style  for  the  descriptions  tag is set.  This is followed by one or two[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              names of arrays followed by options to pass to compadd.  The  array  name1[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              contains  the  possible  completions  with  their descriptions in the form[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `completion:description'.  Any literal colons in completion must be quoted[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with a backslash.  If a name2 is given, it should have the same number  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              elements  as  name1;  in this case the corresponding elements are added as[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              possible completions instead of the completion strings  from  name1.   The[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion  list  will retain the descriptions from name1.  Finally, a set[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of completion options can appear.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the option `-o' appears before the first argument,  the  matches  added[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will be treated as names of command options (N.B. not shell options), typ‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ically  following  a  `-',  `--' or `+' on the command line.  In this case[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _describe uses the prefix-hidden, prefix-needed and verbose styles to find[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              out if the strings should be added as completions and if the  descriptions[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              should  be shown.  Without the `-o' option, only the verbose style is used[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to decide how descriptions are shown.  If `-O' is used  instead  of  `-o',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              command  options  are completed as above but _describe will not handle the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              prefix-needed style.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              With the -t option a tag can be specified.  The default is `values' or, if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the -o option is given, `options'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The options -1, -2, -J, -V, -x are passed to _next_label.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If selected by the list-grouped style, strings with the  same  description[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will appear together in the list.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              _describe  uses  the  _all_labels  function to generate the matches, so it[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              does not need to appear inside a loop over tag labels.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _description [ -x ] [ -12VJ ] tag name descr [ spec ... ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This function is not to be confused with the previous one; it is used as a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              helper function for creating options to compadd.  It is buried inside many[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of the higher level completion functions and so often does not need to  be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              called directly.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  styles listed below are tested in the current context using the given[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tag.  The resulting options for compadd are put into the array named  name[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              (this  is traditionally `expl', but this convention is not enforced).  The[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              description for the corresponding set of matches is passed to the function[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in descr.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The styles tested are: format, hidden, matcher, ignore-line,  ignored-pat‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              terns,  group-name  and  sort.   The  format style is first tested for the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              given tag and then for the descriptions tag if no value was  found,  while[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  remainder  are  only  tested for the tag given as the first argument.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The function also calls _setup which tests some more styles.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The string returned by the format style (if any) will be modified so  that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  sequence  `%d'  is  replaced by the descr given as the third argument[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              without any leading or trailing white space.  If, after removing the white[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              space, the descr is the empty string, the format style will  not  be  used[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and  the  options  put into the name array will not contain an explanation[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              string to be displayed above the matches.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If _description is called with more than three arguments,  the  additional[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              specs  should be of the form `char:str'.  These supply escape sequence re‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              placements for the format style: every appearance of `%char' will  be  re‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              placed by string.  If no additional specs are given but the description in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              descr  conforms to a common form then further escape sequences are set for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              elements of that description.  These  elements  correspond  to  a  default[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              value  (`%o'),  the units (`%m') range of acceptable values (`%r') and the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              remaining initial part of the description (`%h').  The form  the  descrip‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion  takes  consists of specifying the units and range in parentheses and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the default value in square brackets, for example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _description times expl 'timeout (seconds) (0-60) [20]'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              It is possible to use zformat conditional expressions when  styling  these[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              elements.  So, for example, to add `default:' as a tag but only when there[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is a default value to show, the format style might  include  `%(o.default:[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              %o.)'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the -x option is given, the description will be passed to compadd using[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  -x option instead of the default -X.  This means that the description[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will be displayed even if there are no corresponding matches.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The options placed in the array name take account of the group-name style,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              so matches are placed in a separate group where necessary.  The group nor‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mally has its elements sorted (by passing the option -J to  compadd),  but[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              if  an  option  starting  with `-V', `-J', `-1', or `-2' is passed to _de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              scription, that option will be included in the array.  Hence it is  possi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ble  for  the  completion  group to be unsorted by giving the option `-V',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `-1V', or `-2V'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In most cases, the function will be used like this:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     local expl[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     _description files expl file[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     compadd "$expl[@]" - "$files[@]"[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note the use of the parameter expl, the hyphen, and the list  of  matches.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Almost  all  calls  to  compadd within the completion system use a similar[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              format; this ensures that user-specified styles are correctly passed  down[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to the builtins which implement the internals of completion.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _dir_list [ -s sep ] [ -S ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Complete a list of directory names separated by colons (the same format as[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              $PATH).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -s sep Use sep as separator between items.  sep defaults to a colon (`:').[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -S     Add sep instead of slash (`/') as an autoremoveable suffix.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _dispatch context string ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  sets  the  current context to context and looks for completion func‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions to handle this context by hunting through the list of command  names[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              or  special  contexts  (as  described above for compdef) given as strings.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The first completion function to be defined for one of the contexts in the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              list is used to generate matches.  Typically, the last string is -default-[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to cause the function for default completion to be used as a fallback.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The function sets the parameter $service to the string  being  tried,  and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sets  the  context/command field (the fourth) of the $curcontext parameter[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to the context given as the first argument.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _email_addresses [ -c ] [ -n plugin ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Complete email addresses.  Addresses are provided by plugins.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -c     Complete bare localhost@domain.tld addresses, without a  name  part[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     or a comment.  Without this option, RFC822 `Firstname Lastname <ad‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     dress>' strings are completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -n plugin[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     Complete aliases from plugin.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  following plugins are available by default: _email-ldap (see the fil‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ter  style),  _email-local  (completes  user@hostname   Unix   addresses),[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _email-mail  (completes aliases from ~/.mailrc), _email-mush, _email-mutt,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and _email-pine.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Addresses from the _email-foo plugin are added under the tag `email-foo'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Writing plugins[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Plugins are  written  as  separate  functions  with  names  starting  with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `_email-'.  They are invoked with the -c option and compadd options.  They[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              should either do their own completion or set the $reply array to a list of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `alias:address'  elements  and  return 300.  New plugins will be picked up[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and run automatically.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _files The function _files is a wrapper around _path_files. It  supports  all  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the same functionality, with some enhancements -- notably, it respects the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              list-dirs-first  style,  and  it allows users to override the behaviour of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the -g and -/ options with the file-patterns style. _files  should  there‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              fore be preferred over _path_files in most cases.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function accepts the full set of options allowed by _path_files, de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              scribed below.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _gnu_generic[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This function is a simple wrapper around the _arguments function described[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              above.  It can be used to determine automatically the long options  under‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              stood by commands that produce a list when passed the option `--help'.  It[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is  intended  to  be  used  as  a top-level completion function in its own[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              right.  For example, to enable option completion for the commands foo  and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              bar, use[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     compdef _gnu_generic foo bar[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              after the call to compinit.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The completion system as supplied is conservative in its use of this func‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion,  since it is important to be sure the command understands the option[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `--help'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _guard [ options ] pattern descr[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This function displays descr if pattern matches  the  string  to  be  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleted.   It  is  intended to be used in the action for the specifications[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              passed to _arguments and similar functions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The return status is zero if the message was displayed  and  the  word  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              complete is not empty, and non-zero otherwise.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  pattern  may  be preceded by any of the options understood by compadd[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              that are passed down from _description, namely -M, -J, -V, -1, -2, -n,  -F[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and  -X.  All of these options will be ignored.  This fits in conveniently[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with the argument-passing conventions of actions for _arguments.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              As an example, consider a command taking the options -n and  -none,  where[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              -n must be followed by a numeric value in the same word.  By using:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _arguments '-n-: :_guard "[0-9]#" "numeric value"' '-none'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              _arguments  can  be  made  to both display the message `numeric value' and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              complete options after `-n<TAB>'.  If the `-n' is already followed by  one[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              or  more  digits  (the  pattern passed to _guard) only the message will be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              displayed; if the `-n' is followed by another character, only options  are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _message [ -r12 ] [ -VJ group ] descr[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       _message -e [ tag ] descr[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The  descr  is used in the same way as the third argument to the _descrip‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion function, except that the  resulting  string  will  always  be  shown[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              whether  or  not  matches were generated.  This is useful for displaying a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              help message in places where no completions can be generated.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The format style is examined with the messages tag to find a message;  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              usual  tag,  descriptions,  is  used only if the style is not set with the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              former.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the -r option is given, no style is used; the descr is taken  literally[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              as the string to display.  This is most useful when the descr comes from a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pre-processed  argument  list  which already contains an expanded descrip‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion.  Note that this option does not  disable  the  `%'-sequence  parsing[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              done by compadd.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  -12VJ options and the group are passed to compadd and hence determine[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the group the message string is added to.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The second -e form gives a description for completions with the tag tag to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be shown even if there are no matches for that tag.  This form  is  called[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              by  _arguments in the event that there is no action for an option specifi‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cation.  The tag can be omitted and if so the tag is taken from the  para‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              meter  $curtag; this is maintained by the completion system and so is usu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ally correct.  Note that if there are no matches at the time this function[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is called, compstate[insert] is cleared, so additional  matches  generated[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              later are not inserted on the command line.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _multi_parts [ -i ] sep array[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The  argument  sep  is a separator character.  The array may be either the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              name of an array parameter or a literal array in the form `(foo  bar)',  a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              parenthesised list of words separated by whitespace.  The possible comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions  are  the  strings from the array.  However, each chunk delimited by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sep will be completed separately.  For example,  the  _tar  function  uses[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `_multi_parts  /  patharray' to complete partial file paths from the given[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              array of complete file paths.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The -i option causes _multi_parts to insert a unique match  even  if  that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              requires  multiple separators to be inserted.  This is not usually the ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pected behaviour with filenames, but certain other  types  of  completion,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for example those with a fixed set of possibilities, may be more suited to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              this form.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Like  other utility functions, this function accepts the `-V', `-J', `-1',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `-2', `-n', `-f', `-X', `-M', `-P', `-S', `-r', `-R', and `-q' options and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              passes them to the compadd builtin.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _next_label [ -x ] [ -12VJ ] tag name descr [ option ... ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This function is used to implement the loop over different tag labels  for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              a particular tag as described above for the tag-order style.  On each call[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              it  checks to see if there are any more tag labels; if there is it returns[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              status zero, otherwise non-zero.  As this function requires a current  tag[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to be set, it must always follow a call to _tags or _requested.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  -x12VJ  options  and the first three arguments are passed to the _de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              scription function.  Where appropriate the tag will be replaced by  a  tag[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              label  in this call.  Any description given in the tag-order style is pre‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ferred to the descr passed to _next_label.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The options given after the descr are set in the parameter given by  name,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and  hence  are  to be passed to compadd or whatever function is called to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              add the matches.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Here is a typical use of this function for the tag foo.  The call to  _re‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              quested  determines if tag foo is required at all; the loop over _next_la‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              bel handles any labels defined for the tag in the tag-order style.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     local expl ret=1[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     if _requested foo; then[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       while _next_label foo expl '...'; do[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         compadd "$expl[@]" ... && ret=0[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       done[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     fi[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     return ret[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _normal [ -P | -p precommand ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is the standard function called to handle completion outside any spe‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cial -context-.  It is called both to complete the command word  and  also[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the arguments for a command.  In the second case, _normal looks for a spe‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cial completion for that command, and if there is none it uses the comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion for the -default- context.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              A  second use is to reexamine the command line specified by the $words ar‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ray and the $CURRENT parameter after those have been modified.  For  exam‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ple, the function _precommand, which completes after precommand specifiers[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              such as nohup, removes the first word from the words array, decrements the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              CURRENT  parameter,  then calls `_normal -p $service'.  The effect is that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `nohup cmd ...' is treated in the same way as `cmd ...'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -P     Reset the list of precommands. This option should be used  if  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     pleting  a  command  line  which  allows  internal  commands  (e.g.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     builtins and functions) regardless of prior precommands (e.g.  `zsh[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     -c').[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -p precommand[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     Append precommand to the list of precommands. This option should be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     used in nearly all cases in which -P is not applicable.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the  command  name matches one of the patterns given by one of the op‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions -p or -P to compdef, the corresponding completion function is called[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and then the parameter _compskip is checked.  If it is set  completion  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              terminated  at that point even if no matches have been found.  This is the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              same effect as in the -first- context.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _numbers [ option ... ] [ description ] [ suffix ... ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This can be used where a number is followed by a suffix  to  indicate  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              units.   The  unit  suffixes are completed and can also be included in the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              description used when completion is invoked for the preceding number.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In addition to common compadd options, _numbers accepts the following  op‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tions:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -t tag Specify a tag to use instead of the default of numbers.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -u units[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     Indicate the default units for the number, e.g. bytes.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -l min Specify the lowest possible value for the number.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -m max Specify the highest possible value for the number.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -d default[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     Specify the default value.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -N     Allow  negative  numbers.   This is implied if the range includes a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     negative.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -f     Allow decimal numbers.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Where a particular suffix represents the default units for  a  number,  it[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              should  be  prefixed with a colon.  Additionally, suffixes can be followed[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              by a colon and a description.  So for example, the  following  allows  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              age  of  something  to be specified, either in seconds or with an optional[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              suffix with a longer unit of time:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _numbers -u seconds age :s:seconds m:minutes h:hours d:days[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              It is typically helpful for units to be presented in  order  of  magnitude[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              when  completed.  To facilitate this, the order in which they are given is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              preserved.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              When the format style is looked up with the descriptions tag  or  the  tag[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              specified  with -t, the list of suffixes is available as a `%x' escape se‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              quence. This is in addition to the usual sequences  documented  under  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              format  style.  The  form  this list takes can also be configured. To this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              end, the format style is first looked up with the tag  unit-suffixes.  The[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              retrieved  format  is  applied  to each suffix in turn and the results are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              then concatenated to form the completed list. For the  unit-suffixes  for‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mat,  `%x'  expands  to the individual suffix and `%X' to its description.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              %d' indicates a default suffix and can be used in a condition.  The  index[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and reverse index are set in `%i' and `%r' respectively and are useful for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              text  included  only  with the first and last suffixes in the list. So for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              example, the following joins the suffixes together  as  a  comma-separated[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              list:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     zstyle ':completion:*:unit-suffixes' format '%x%(r::,)'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _options[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  can  be  used to complete the names of shell options.  It provides a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matcher specification that ignores a leading `no', ignores underscores and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              allows upper-case letters to match their lower-case counterparts (for  ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ample,  `glob', `noglob', `NO_GLOB' are all completed).  Any arguments are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              propagated to the compadd builtin.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _options_set and _options_unset[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              These functions complete only set or unset options, with the same matching[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              specification used in the _options function.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note that you need to uncomment a few lines in the _main_complete function[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for these functions to work properly.  The lines in question are  used  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              store  the  option settings in effect before the completion widget locally[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sets the options it needs.  Hence these functions are not  generally  used[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              by the completion system.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _parameters[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is used to complete the names of shell parameters.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  option  `-g  pattern'  limits the completion to parameters whose type[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matches the pattern.  The type of a parameter  is  that  shown  by  `print[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ${(t)param}', hence judicious use of `*' in pattern is probably necessary.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              All other arguments are passed to the compadd builtin.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _path_files[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  is used throughout the completion system to complete file‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              names.  It allows completion of partial paths.  For  example,  the  string[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `/u/i/s/sig' may be completed to `/usr/include/sys/signal.h'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The options accepted by both _path_files and _files are:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -f     Complete all filenames.  This is the default.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -/     Specifies that only directories should be completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -g pattern[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     Specifies that only files matching the pattern should be completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -W paths[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     Specifies path prefixes that are to be prepended to the string from[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     the  command  line to generate the filenames but that should not be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     inserted as completions nor shown in  completion  listings.   Here,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     paths  may  be  the  name  of an array parameter, a literal list of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     paths enclosed in parentheses or an absolute pathname.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              -F ignored-files[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     This behaves  as  for  the  corresponding  option  to  the  compadd[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     builtin.   It  gives  direct control over which filenames should be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     ignored.  If the option is not present, the ignored-patterns  style[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     is used.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Both  _path_files  and  _files also accept the following options which are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              passed to compadd: `-J', `-V', `-1', `-2', `-n', `-X', `-M',  `-P',  `-S',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `-q', `-r', and `-R'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Finally, the _path_files function  uses the styles expand, ambiguous, spe‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cial-dirs, list-suffixes and file-sort described above.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _pick_variant [ -b builtin-label ] [ -c command ] [ -r name ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     label=pattern ... label [ arg ... ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  is  used to resolve situations where a single command name[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              requires more than one type of handling, either because it has  more  than[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              one  variant  or  because there is a name clash between two different com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mands.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The command to run is taken from the first element of the array words  un‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              less  this  is  overridden  by the option -c.  This command is run and its[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              output is compared with a series of patterns.  Arguments to be  passed  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  command  can  be  specified at the end after all the other arguments.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The patterns to try in order are given by the arguments label=pattern;  if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  output  of `command arg ...' contains pattern, then label is selected[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              as the label for the command variant.  If none of the patterns match,  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              final command label is selected and status 1 is returned.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the `-b builtin-label' is given, the command is tested to see if it is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              provided as a  shell  builtin,  possibly  autoloaded;  if  so,  the  label[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              builtin-label is selected as the label for the variant.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  the  `-r  name'  is given, the label picked is stored in the parameter[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              named name.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The results are also cached in the _cmd_variant associative array  indexed[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              by the name of the command run.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _regex_arguments name spec ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This function generates a completion function name which matches the spec‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ifications  specs, a set of regular expressions as described below.  After[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              running _regex_arguments, the function name should be called as  a  normal[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              completion  function.   The pattern to be matched is given by the contents[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              of the words array up to the current cursor position joined together  with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              null characters; no quotation is applied.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  arguments are grouped as sets of alternatives separated by `|', which[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              are tried one after the other until one matches.   Each  alternative  con‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sists  of a one or more specifications which are tried left to right, with[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              each pattern matched being stripped in turn from the  command  line  being[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tested,  until all of the group succeeds or until one fails; in the latter[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              case, the next alternative is tried.  This structure can  be  repeated  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              arbitrary  depth  by  using  parentheses; matching proceeds from inside to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              outside.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              A special procedure is applied if no test succeeds but the remaining  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mand  line  string contains no null character (implying the remaining word[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is the one for which completions are to  be  generated).   The  completion[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              target  is restricted to the remaining word and any actions for the corre‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sponding patterns are executed.  In this case, nothing  is  stripped  from[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  command  line  string.  The order of evaluation of the actions can be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              determined by the tag-order style; the various formats supported  by  _al‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ternative can be used in action.  The descr is used for setting up the ar‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ray parameter expl.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Specification  arguments take one of following forms, in which metacharac‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ters such as `(', `)', `#' and `|' should be quoted.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              /pattern/ [%lookahead%] [-guard] [:tag:descr:action][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     This is a single primitive component.  The function  tests  whether[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     the combined pattern `(#b)((#B)pattern)lookahead*' matches the com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     mand  line string.  If so, `guard' is evaluated and its return sta‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     tus is examined to determine if the test has succeeded.   The  pat‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     tern  string  `[]'  is guaranteed never to match.  The lookahead is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     not stripped from the command line before the next pattern is exam‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     ined.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     The argument starting with : is used in the same manner as an argu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     ment to _alternative.[0m
