[38;2;248;248;242m                     A component is used as follows: pattern is tested  to  see  if  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     component already exists on the command line.  If it does, any fol‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     lowing  specifications  are examined to find something to complete.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     If a component is reached but no such pattern  exists  yet  on  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     command  line, the string containing the action is used to generate[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     matches to insert at that point.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              /pattern/+ [%lookahead%] [-guard] [:tag:descr:action][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     This is similar to `/pattern/ ...' but the left part of the command[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     line string (i.e. the part already matched by previous patterns) is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     also considered part of the completion target.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              /pattern/- [%lookahead%] [-guard] [:tag:descr:action][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     This is similar to `/pattern/ ...' but the actions of  the  current[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     and  previously  matched patterns are ignored even if the following[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     `pattern' matches the empty string.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              ( spec )[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     Parentheses may be used to groups specs; note each parenthesis is a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     single argument to _regex_arguments.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              spec # This allows any number of repetitions of spec.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              spec spec[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     The two specs are to be matched one after the  other  as  described[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     above.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              spec | spec[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     Either of the two specs can be matched.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  function  _regex_words  can  be used as a helper function to generate[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matches for a set of alternative words possibly with their  own  arguments[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              as a command line argument.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Examples:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _regex_arguments _tst /$'[^\0]#\0'/ \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         /$'[^\0]#\0'/ :'compadd aaa'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This  generates  a  function _tst that completes aaa as its only argument.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The tag and description for the action have been omitted for brevity (this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              works but is not recommended in normal use).  The first component  matches[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  command  word,  which is arbitrary; the second matches  any argument.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              As the argument is also arbitrary, any following component would  not  de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pend on aaa being present.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _regex_arguments _tst /$'[^\0]#\0'/ \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         /$'aaa\0'/ :'compadd aaa'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is  a  more  typical  use; it is similar, but any following patterns[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              would only match if aaa was present as the first argument.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _regex_arguments _tst /$'[^\0]#\0'/ \( \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         /$'aaa\0'/ :'compadd aaa' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         /$'bbb\0'/ :'compadd bbb' \) \#[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              In this example, an indefinite number of command  arguments  may  be  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleted.   Odd  arguments  are  completed as aaa and even arguments as bbb.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Completion fails unless the set of aaa and bbb arguments before  the  cur‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rent one is matched correctly.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _regex_arguments _tst /$'[^\0]#\0'/ \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         \( /$'aaa\0'/ :'compadd aaa' \| \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         /$'bbb\0'/ :'compadd bbb' \) \#[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This  is similar, but either aaa or bbb may be completed for any argument.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              In this case _regex_words could be used to generate a suitable  expression[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for the arguments.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _regex_words tag description spec ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  can be used to generate arguments for the _regex_arguments[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              command which may be inserted at any point where a set  of  rules  is  ex‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pected.   The tag and description give a standard tag and description per‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              taining to the current context.  Each spec contains two or three arguments[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              separated by a colon: note that there is no leading colon in this case.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Each spec gives one of a set of words that may be completed at this point,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              together with arguments.  It is thus roughly equivalent to the  _arguments[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function when used in normal (non-regex) completion.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  part  of the spec before the first colon is the word to be completed.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This may contain a *; the entire word, before and  after  the  *  is  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              pleted,  but  only the text before the * is required for the context to be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matched, so that further arguments may be completed after the  abbreviated[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              form.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The second part of spec is a description for the word being completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  optional third part of the spec describes how words following the one[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              being completed are themselves to be completed.  It will be  evaluated  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              order  to  avoid problems with quoting.  This means that typically it con‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tains a reference to an array containing previously generated regex  argu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ments.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  option  -t  term  specifies  a terminator for the word instead of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              usual space.  This is handled as an auto-removable suffix in the manner of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the option -s sep to _values.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The result of the processing by _regex_words is placed in the array reply,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              which should be made local to the calling function.  If the set  of  words[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and  arguments  may  be  matched repeatedly, a # should be appended to the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              generated array at that point.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              For example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     local -a reply[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     _regex_words mydb-commands 'mydb commands' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       'add:add an entry to mydb:$mydb_add_cmds' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       'show:show entries in mydb'[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     _regex_arguments _mydb "$reply[@]"[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     _mydb "$@"[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This shows a completion function for a command mydb which takes  two  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mand  arguments,  add  and show.  show takes no arguments, while the argu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ments for add have already been prepared in an array mydb_add_cmds,  quite[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              possibly by a previous call to _regex_words.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _requested [ -x ] [ -12VJ ] tag [ name descr [ command [ arg ... ] ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  is  called to decide whether a tag already registered by a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              call to _tags (see below) has been requested by the user and hence comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion should be performed for it.  It returns status zero if the tag is re‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              quested and non-zero otherwise.  The function is typically used as part of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              a loop over different tags as follows:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _tags foo bar baz[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     while _tags; do[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       if _requested foo; then[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         ... # perform completion for foo[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       fi[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       ... # test the tags bar and baz in the same way[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       ... # exit loop if matches were generated[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     done[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note that the test for whether matches were generated is not performed un‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              til the end of the _tags loop.  This is so  that  the  user  can  set  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tag-order style to specify a set of tags to be completed at the same time.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  name  and  descr are given, _requested calls the _description function[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with these arguments together with the options passed to _requested.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If command is given, the _all_labels function will be  called  immediately[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with  the  same arguments.  In simple cases this makes it possible to per‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              form the test for the tag and the matching in one go.  For example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     local expl ret=1[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     _tags foo bar baz[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     while _tags; do[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       _requested foo expl 'description' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                           compadd foobar foobaz && ret=0[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                       (( ret )) || break[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     done[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the command is not compadd, it must nevertheless be prepared to  handle[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the same options.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _retrieve_cache cache_identifier[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  retrieves  completion  information  from the file given by[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              cache_identifier, stored in a directory specified by the cache-path  style[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              which  defaults  to ~/.zcompcache.  The return status is zero if retrieval[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              was successful.  It will only attempt retrieval if the use-cache style  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              set, so you can call this function without worrying about whether the user[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              wanted to use the caching layer.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              See _store_cache below for more details.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _sep_parts[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  is  passed alternating arrays and separators as arguments.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The arrays specify completions for parts of strings to be separated by the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              separators.  The arrays may be the names of array parameters or  a  quoted[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              list  of  words  in  parentheses.  For example, with the array `hosts=(ftp[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              news)' the call `_sep_parts '(foo bar)' @ hosts' will complete the  string[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `f' to `foo' and the string `b@n' to `bar@news'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  accepts  the compadd options `-V', `-J', `-1', `-2', `-n',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `-X', `-M', `-P', `-S', `-r', `-R', and `-q' and passes  them  on  to  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              compadd builtin used to add the matches.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _sequence [ -s sep ] [ -n max ] [ -d ] function [ - ] ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function  is  a wrapper to other functions for completing items in a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              separated list. The same function is used to complete  each  item  in  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              list.  The  separator is specified with the -s option. If -s is omitted it[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will use `,'. Duplicate values are not matched unless -d is specified.  If[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              there is a fixed or maximum number of items in the list, this can be spec‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ified with the -n option.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Common  compadd  options  are passed on to the function. It is possible to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              use compadd directly with _sequence, though _values may be more  appropri‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ate in this situation.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _setup tag [ group ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This function sets up the special parameters used by the completion system[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              appropriately for the tag given as the first argument.  It uses the styles[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              list-colors, list-packed, list-rows-first, last-prompt, accept-exact, menu[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and force-list.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  optional  group  supplies  the name of the group in which the matches[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              will be placed.  If it is not given, the tag is used as the group name.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This function is called automatically from _description and hence  is  not[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              normally called explicitly.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _store_cache cache_identifier param ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  function,  together  with _retrieve_cache and _cache_invalid, imple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ments a caching layer which can be used in any completion function.   Data[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              obtained by costly operations are stored in parameters; this function then[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              dumps  the values of those parameters to a file.  The data can then be re‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              trieved quickly from that file via _retrieve_cache, even in different  in‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              stances of the shell.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  cache_identifier  specifies  the file which the data should be dumped[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to.  The file is stored in a directory specified by the  cache-path  style[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              which  defaults  to ~/.zcompcache.  The remaining params arguments are the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              parameters to dump to the file.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The return status is zero if storage was successful.   The  function  will[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              only  attempt  storage if the use-cache style is set, so you can call this[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function without worrying about whether the user wanted to use the caching[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              layer.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The completion function may avoid calling _retrieve_cache when it  already[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              has the completion data available as parameters.  However, in that case it[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              should call _cache_invalid to check whether the data in the parameters and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              in the cache are still valid.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              See  the _perl_modules completion function for a simple example of the us‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              age of the caching layer.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _tags [ [ -C name ] tag ... ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              If called with arguments, these are taken to be the names  of  tags  valid[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for  completions in the current context.  These tags are stored internally[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and sorted by using the tag-order style.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Next, _tags is called repeatedly without arguments from the  same  comple‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tion  function.   This successively selects the first, second, etc. set of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tags requested by the user.  The return status is zero if at least one  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the tags is requested and non-zero otherwise.  To test if a particular tag[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is to be tried, the _requested function should be called (see above).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If  `-C  name'  is given, name is temporarily stored in the argument field[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              (the fifth) of the context in the curcontext parameter during the call  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _tags;  the  field  is  restored on exit.  This allows _tags to use a more[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              specific context without having to change and reset the curcontext parame‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ter (which has the same effect).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _tilde_files[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Like _files, but resolve leading tildes according to the rules of filename[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              expansion, so the suggested completions don't start with a `~' even if the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              filename on the command-line does.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _values [ -O name ] [ -s sep ] [ -S sep ] [ -wC ] desc spec ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This is used to complete arbitrary keywords (values) and their  arguments,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              or lists of such combinations.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the first argument is the option `-O name', it will be used in the same[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              way  as  by  the _arguments function.  In other words, the elements of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              name array will be passed to compadd when executing an action.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              If the first argument (or the first argument after `-O name') is `-s', the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              next argument is used as the character  that  separates  multiple  values.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This  character  is automatically added after each value in an auto-remov‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              able fashion (see below); all values completed by `_values -s'  appear  in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the same word on the command line, unlike completion using _arguments.  If[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              this  option  is  not  present,  only a single value will be completed per[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              word.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Normally, _values will only use the current word to determine which values[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              are already present on the command line and hence are not to be  completed[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              again.  If the -w option is given, other arguments are examined as well.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The first non-option argument, desc, is used as a string to print as a de‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              scription before listing the values.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              All  other  arguments  describe the possible values and their arguments in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the same format used for the description  of  options  by  the  _arguments[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function (see above).  The only differences are that no minus or plus sign[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is  required  at the beginning, values can have only one argument, and the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              forms of action beginning with an equal sign are not supported.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The character separating a value from its argument can be  set  using  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              option  -S  (like -s, followed by the character to use as the separator in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the next argument).  By default the equals sign will be used as the  sepa‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rator between values and arguments.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Example:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     _values -s , 'description' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                             '*foo[bar]' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                             '(two)*one[number]:first count:' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                             'two[another number]::second count:(1 2 3)'[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              This  describes three possible values: `foo', `one', and `two'.  The first[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is described as `bar', takes no argument and may appear  more  than  once.[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The  second is described as `number', may appear more than once, and takes[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              one mandatory argument described as `first count'; no action is specified,[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              so it will not be completed.  The `(two)' at the beginning  says  that  if[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  value `one' is on the line, the value `two' will no longer be consid‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ered a possible completion.  Finally, the last value (`two') is  described[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              as  `another  number'  and takes an optional argument described as `second[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              count' for which the completions (to appear after an `=')  are  `1',  `2',[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              and  `3'.   The _values function will complete lists of these values sepa‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rated by commas.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Like _arguments, this function temporarily adds another context name  com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ponent  to  the arguments element (the fifth) of the current context while[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              executing the action.  Here this name is just the name of  the  value  for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              which the argument is completed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  style  verbose  is  used to decide if the descriptions for the values[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              (but not those for the arguments) should be printed.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The associative array val_args is used to report values  and  their  argu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ments; this works similarly to the opt_args associative array used by _ar‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              guments.   Hence the function calling _values should declare the local pa‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rameters state, state_descr, line, context and val_args:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     local context state state_descr line[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     typeset -A val_args[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              when using an action of the form `->string'.  With this function the  con‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              text  parameter  will be set to the name of the value whose argument is to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              be completed.  Note that  for  _values,  the  state  and  state_descr  are[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              scalars rather than arrays.  Only a single matching state is returned.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note  also  that _values normally adds the character used as the separator[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              between values as an auto-removable suffix (similar to a `/' after  a  di‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              rectory).   However,  this  is not possible for a `->string' action as the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matches for the argument are generated by the calling  function.   To  get[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              the  usual  behaviour,  the  calling function can add the separator x as a[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              suffix by passing the options `-qS x' either  directly  or  indirectly  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              compadd.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  option -C is treated in the same way as it is by _arguments.  In that[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              case the parameter curcontext should be made local instead of context  (as[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              described above).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _wanted [ -x ] [ -C name ]  [ -12VJ ] tag name descr command [ arg ...][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              In  many  contexts,  completion  can  only  generate one particular set of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              matches, usually corresponding to a single tag.  However, it is still nec‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              essary to decide whether the user requires matches  of  this  type.   This[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              function is useful in such a case.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              The  arguments  to _wanted are the same as those to _requested, i.e. argu‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ments to be passed to _description.  However, in this case the command  is[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              not  optional;   all  the processing of tags, including the loop over both[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tags and tag labels and the generation of matches, is carried out automat‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ically by _wanted.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Hence to offer only one tag and immediately add the corresponding  matches[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              with the given description:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m                     local expl[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                     _wanted tag expl 'description' \[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m                         compadd -- match1 match2...[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              See also the use of _wanted in the example function in the subsection `Dy‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              namic named directories' in zshexpn(1).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Note  that,  as for _requested, the command must be able to accept options[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              to be passed down to compadd.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m              Like _tags this function supports the -C option to give a  different  name[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              for the argument context field.  The -x option has the same meaning as for[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _description.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _widgets [ -g pattern ][0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              This function completes names of zle widgets (see the section `Widgets' in[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              zshzle(1)).   The  pattern,  if  present, is matched against values of the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              $widgets special parameter, documented in the section `The  zsh/zleparame‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ter Module' in zshmodules(1).[0m

[38;2;248;248;242mCOMPLETION SYSTEM VARIABLES[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       There are some standard variables, initialised by the _main_complete function and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       then used from other functions.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       The standard variables are:[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _comp_caller_options[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              The  completion system uses setopt to set a number of options. This allows[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              functions to be written without concern for compatibility with every  pos‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              sible  combination of user options. However, sometimes completion needs to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              know what the user's option  preferences  are.  These  are  saved  in  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              _comp_caller_options associative array. Option names, spelled in lowercase[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              without  underscores,  are  mapped to one or other of the strings `on' and[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              `off'.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       _comp_priv_prefix[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Completion functions such as _sudo can set the _comp_priv_prefix array  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              a command prefix that may then be used by _call_program to match the priv‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              ileges when calling programs to generate matches.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Two  more  features are offered by the _main_complete function.  The arrays comp‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       prefuncs and comppostfuncs may contain names of functions that are to  be  called[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       immediately  before  or after completion has been tried.  A function will only be[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       called once unless it explicitly reinserts itself into the array.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242mCOMPLETION DIRECTORIES[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       In the source distribution, the files are contained in various subdirectories  of[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       the Completion directory.  They may have been installed in the same structure, or[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       into  one single function directory.  The following is a description of the files[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       found in the original directory structure.  If you wish  to  alter  an  installed[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       file,  you  will  need to copy it to some directory which appears earlier in your[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m       fpath than the standard directory where it appears.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Base   The core functions and special completion widgets automatically  bound  to[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              keys.   You  will  certainly  need most of these, though will probably not[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              need to alter them.  Many of these are documented above.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Zsh    Functions for completing arguments of shell builtin commands  and  utility[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              functions  for  this.   Some  of these are also used by functions from the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Unix directory.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       Unix   Functions for completing arguments of external commands and suites of com‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              mands.  They may need modifying for your system, although  in  many  cases[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              some attempt is made to decide which version of a command is present.  For[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              example, completion for the mount command tries to determine the system it[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              is  running  on,  while  completion for many other utilities try to decide[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              whether the GNU version of the command is in use, and  hence  whether  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              --help option is supported.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242m       X, AIX, BSD, ...[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Completion  and  utility function for commands available only on some sys‐[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              tems.  These are not arranged hierarchically, so, for  example,  both  the[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              Linux and Debian directories, as well as the X directory, may be useful on[0m
[38;2;248;248;242m              your system.[0m

[38;2;248;248;242mzsh 5.9                               May 14, 2022                         ZSHCOMPSYS(1)[0m
